- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-11-04T02:33:12+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8jd6kqFr23U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<6580fb58-bb96-47f8-93b4-c4e4f8573b4b@j2g2000yqf.googlegroups.com> <iapquv$bf$1@news.eternal-september.org> <38bc19b1-234f-4828-95e0-b5512e9e3f22@d8g2000yqf.googlegroups.com>`

```
HansJ wrote:
> On 2 Nov., 21:05, Kerry Liles
> <"kerry.liles[minus_the_spam]"@gmail.com> wrote:
>> On 11/2/2010 3:44 PM, foodman wrote:
>>

Please note: My responses to triple chevronned posts are to Foodman, not to 
Hans.

>>> It probably won't help, but I sent a complaint about the trash
>>> people are posting to CLC.

People have been posting trash here for decades. You are one of the worst 
offenders.


>>> It would be a simple job for Google to exclude this junk, why don't
>>> they?

Er... because they understand USENET better than you do?

>>
>>> It would not hurt for as many people as possible to complain.

Yes it would. Google may drop the relay.

I strongly urge people NOT to complain about this. See below.


>>
>>> Here's the link.
<link snipped>

>>> tony dilworth
>>
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> answering to older posts that move forward then.

General response to all follows...

SPAM always sucks. That's why you filter it on your personal system.

Here you can't (well, you CAN, but it is much more difficult and depends on 
which news client you are using to read the group...)

How hard is it to decide if a topic is about COBOL before opening it?

This is an unmoderated newsgroup as Kerry already observed.

In my opinion, that is such a valuable thing that I wouldn't want to see it 
changed.

Newsgroups such as this are fast becoming the last bastions of free speech 
on the planet. There are no vested interests who can censor what goes here, 
no particular political persuasion, no pressure groups, just an open 
platform where people can say anything they like.

It doesn't have to be palatable or politically correct, and on many 
occasions, it isn't. It will offend some and irritate some, and bore some 
and interest some, but that is what makes it valuable.

Like all Freedoms, the Freedom of Speech does not come free. Most of us have 
lived in Democratic societies so long we take it for granted and forget that 
people actually died to get us the right to speak our minds and not have our 
thoughts governed by the "thought Police"

The price is twofold:

1. You need to be mature enough to realise that everything you find here 
won't be what you want to see.
2.  You need to be tolerant enough NOT to complain about what happens in an 
open, unmoderated forum. (Don't like it? Don't come here. Pretty simple 
really...)

Tony's complaint could lead to Google dropping the group from their relays 
and that means that anyone using Google to post here or read it, will no 
longer be able to. It will NOT cause the content of the group to change in 
any way, and that includes SPAM.

The nature opf this particular forum is that it is about things connected 
to, or involving, COBOL. (A "shared interest" of the people who frequent the 
group. Anything else should be marked OT (Off Topic) as indeed, this thread 
should have been when it was originated.)

Most people who come here regularly observe common courtesy and generally 
follow the OT rule so that people who are here ONLY for the COBOL-related 
stuff can skip threads that are not likely to be of interest to them. 
(Personally, I find the OT posts usually much more interesting than the 
COBOL ones, but that's just me.)

NONE of us enjoy or want to wade through SPAM.

BUT, if you are going to have an unmoderated, open forum, then there will be 
people with no interest in COBOL (or anything much else, really) who will do 
blanket posts to ALL USENET forums, and that will include this one.

Deal with it.

It really isn't hard to see immediately what is SPAM and ignore it.

Pete.
```

On Fri, 29 Oct 2010 14:57:59 -0500, "Bill Klein"
<wmklein@noreply.ix.netcom.com> wrote:

>"Clark Morris" <cfmpublic@ns.sympatico.ca> wrote in message 
>news:cjh9c691b5rfaaj1rgqn5l90qjbe7nfvon@4ax.com...
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>been accepted for COBOL (by IBM).

The general COBOL using community probably uses little or no HFP
(COMP-1 and COMP-2) which I suspect was there primarily for
compatibility with FORTRAN.  The need for BFP (defined by the 2002
USAGES) again would probably be of little interest to the average CICS
or batch COBOL shop.  However, for anything that in new world (C/C++,
Java, etc.) not having BFP poses a potential interoperability problem
that is only partially fixed by the conversion kludge when calling
Java.  This is because the kludge does nothing for data that is
accessed directly by both COBOL and other languages.  Since I have had
nothing to do with mainframe related web page serving or handling of
graphics (catalogs, retail order sites, etc.), I don't know how much
floating point means in those environments.  Does SAP use floating
point?  Do other business packages use binary floating point?  It is
kind of a sleeper issue that would probably cause the MEGO (My Eyes
Glaze Over) effect on most CFOs and CEOs and maybe some CIOs.  If Pete
is right about the increasing irrelevance of COBOL and I can make an
excellent case for that view, then ignoring BFP makes good sense.  If
in the mainframe arena COBOL still has a future, then given the
investment IBM has made in z series BFP floating point performance
somebody hasn't gotten the IBM strategic message.  The need is not BFP
per se.  The need is to handle all data created by other languages and
packages where COBOL will be using that data and to pass data to
programs and packages in those languages.  If IBM doesn't use the 2xxx
COBOL Standard usages for DFP someone should get serious flack.
>
>As far as general "enhancements" to COBOL, it is my impression (nothing 
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>support.
So long as it is as well supported as it is in C/C++ (compiler and
binder option is fine), that is all I would care about were I still
employed in the field.  It just has to live in 64 bit CICS if and when
that is implemented, live nicely in 64 bit Websphere and play nicely
with 64 bit DB2.
>
>As always, IBM has (and continues) to enhance its mainframe COBOL compiler 
>based on their understanding of what their current customers actually need 
>and want (i.e. "real world business cases"). 
>
What customers need and want is tactics.  Given the conservative
nature of the COBOL end of many shops (hanging on to COBOL VS (74) and
VS COBOL II with the forbidding of use of many of the newer
constructs, maybe strategic planning is money ill spent.  Implementing
BFP would be a strategic move to enable COBOL to handle data available
on the platform just as implementing USAGE NATIONAL and Unicode was
strategic.  I doubt there was or is that much clamor for either in
most shops but I definitely agree with the decision to do so.  

In the shop where I spent most of my career, 3 of our major files
contained bit switches (customer, product and open account).  So far
as I know there never was any thought given to having COBOL support a
USAGE BIT even though it would have eliminated the need for assembler
routines.  As a systems programmer working with the SMF records and
other system records, both USAGE BIT and USAGE BINARY-CHARACTER would
have been very useful.  I got around the limitations but it was a pain
and a source of modest obscurity.  

If these points are worth making, could you pass them on reworded for
acceptability as you see fit.

Clark Morris

PS.   Please say hello to Chuck Stevens for me.  I miss his off topic
but always enlightening theological comments.  Some of the best
theological discussions that I have been a part of were on
comp.lang.cobol.   I have saved some of Chuck's postings and would
probably make a special point to attend any Biblical discussion held
in mainland Nova Scotia that he is a participant in.
```

```
Clark F Morris wrote:
> On Fri, 29 Oct 2010 14:57:59 -0500, "Bill Klein"
> <wmklein@noreply.ix.netcom.com> wrote:
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
> point?

Yes and no...

SAP these days is "tailored" through an API which uses a language called 
ABAP. This is an OO language which supports Classes and Objects so data 
types can be defined in it. It uses a Dictionary to define basic types but 
you can also define data types "on-the-fly" or say you want them based on a 
previously defined object. Numeric types can specify how many decimals are 
required, so there is no real need for floating point, but you COULD define 
a floating point type if you wanted to.

Generally, the "non-COBOL" languages differentiate between "real" and 
"integer" numbers, using floating point for real, but you can define fixed 
point decimal numeric fields as well.


>  Do other business packages use binary floating point?  It is
> kind of a sleeper issue that would probably cause the MEGO (My Eyes
> Glaze Over) effect on most CFOs and CEOs and maybe some CIOs.  If Pete
> is right about the increasing irrelevance of COBOL and I can make an
> excellent case for that view, then ignoring BFP makes good sense.

Obviously, I think I'm right, and that opinion is based on what I observe, 
and conversations I have with people. However, my world is not that of 
mainframe COBOL and the situation there may be a little different...



> If
> in the mainframe arena COBOL still has a future, then given the
> investment IBM has made in z series BFP floating point performance
> somebody hasn't gotten the IBM strategic message.

I think that in this world, COBOL still has a future, but it is a limited 
one, not a long term one. I said 2015 and that has almost come true already, 
with many sites that were once mainframe now networked, and more planning 
the move. But I think it is fair to say there will be SOME mainframe shops 
still using COBOL in 2015. (In 2020?  VERY few I think.)

As far as the "IBM strategic message" goes, I think at a senior level they 
will be keeping a close eye on things. Their straegy will vary depending on 
who is at the helm and how they perceive things and interpret the figures. 
As a sometime IBMer I can say they are generally not a stupid company, and 
lessons from the past where they didn't take note, have been learned.

Put yourself in the place of a senior IBM manager having to decide on 
investment in COBOL... You know it is untenable long term, you know that the 
user base has to be weaned off it because the R & D poured into it is just 
money not well spent, but you can't pull the plug overnight. There has to be 
a viable exit strategy. (probably involving a move to Objects and Layers 
through Java, maybe using middleware and SOA. If you can hang in there long 
enough, it will resolve itself as the current base gradually realises they 
are being left behind if they cling to COBOL and will start moving off it 
themselves, but you don't want them lost to MicroFocus and Fujitsu in the 
meantime.

Under these circumstances you probably invest in middleware, web services, 
SOA, and promoting the exit strategy. COBOL is not perceived as being part 
of the "Brave New World", and although you don't confirm this directly, 
anyone who "follows the money" will come to recognise it...

The need is not BFP
> per se.  The need is to handle all data created by other languages and
> packages where COBOL will be using that data and to pass data to
> programs and packages in those languages.  If IBM doesn't use the 2xxx
> COBOL Standard usages for DFP someone should get serious flack.

They would if COBOL was a major pillar in the strategic plan. If it isn't, 
then they won't because it simply doesn't matter. Instead of COBOL 
co-existing and sending and receiving data to the other languages, it will 
simply be subsumed by them.

I would be very surprised to see any significant enhancement in IBM COBOL 
(including implementation of the 2002 standard) arfter the end of 2012.

It isn't that they are "anti-COBOL"; it is just business and survival.  (In 
actuality, COBOL can be perceived as a millstone round their neck. If they 
could get shot of it they could redirect the focus of their customer base 
onto newer and more powerful products, and they would have more funds to get 
these products to market sooner rather than later.
>>
>> As far as general "enhancements" to COBOL, it is my impression
>> (nothing formal) that at recent SHARE meetings, IBM has indicated an
>> intent to signficcantly enhance the COBOL compiler/run-time in the
>> foreseeable future.

But no details or dates...  Doesn't that sound a bit like oil on troubled 
waters?

>Futhremore, it is my UNOOFFICIAL opinion, that
>> this will include AMDOE(64) support in SOME way, but probably NOT as
>> "transparently" as 24-/31-bit support.

Support for AMODE(64) sounds very sensible because it spills over into other 
thngs as well.


> So long as it is as well supported as it is in C/C++ (compiler and
> binder option is fine), that is all I would care about were I still
> employed in the field.  It just has to live in 64 bit CICS if and when
> that is implemented, live nicely in 64 bit Websphere and play nicely
> with 64 bit DB2.

And it is for all those reasons that it has a priority over other (COBOL 
specific) development.

I rest my case... :-)

>>
>> As always, IBM has (and continues) to enhance its mainframe COBOL
>> compiler based on their understanding of what their current
>> customers actually need and want (i.e. "real world business cases").

Brave words. But I see no specifics...  If their "current customers actually 
need and want" to move to distributed computing through middleware and 
networking (Websphere, SOA, web services, etc) there is no real need for 
them to enhance COBOL. Who decides? The ones who want to retan the status 
quo and keep on batch processing as they always have, or the ones who are 
happy to embrace the exit strategy and move off COBOL? Given the one that 
IBM would prefer, it isn't hard to see which way that vote will go...

>>
> What customers need and want is tactics.  Given the conservative
> nature of the COBOL end of many shops (hanging on to COBOL VS (74) and
> VS COBOL II with the forbidding of use of many of the newer
> constructs, maybe strategic planning is money ill spent.

That seems eminently reasonable to me.


> Implementing
> BFP would be a strategic move to enable COBOL to handle data available
> on the platform just as implementing USAGE NATIONAL and Unicode was
> strategic.  I doubt there was or is that much clamor for either in
> most shops but I definitely agree with the decision to do so.

There was HUGE clamour for USAGE NATIONAL and Unicode in the world's two 
largest bastions of COBOL: India and China. There is still a huge amount of 
COBOL development going on in India particularly, much of it outsourced from 
the West. China doesn't make a noise about it but they are also into COBOL 
in a big way. However, in both of these emerging economies programmers are 
starting to realise the real money is in other more modern languages and 
they are seeing the same trends we have seen, but at a faster rate than was 
the case in the West.

>
> In the shop where I spent most of my career, 3 of our major files
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> and a source of modest obscurity.

As a young BAL programmer used to these facilities I also remember moaning 
about them not being available in COBOL. It was suggested to me that this 
was a selling point for COBOL an that removing reliance on esoteric binary 
semaphores was a Very Good Thing :-) Oddly enough, in some code I posted 
here a while back: 
http://groups.google.vu/group/comp.lang.cobol/browse_thread/thread/e5d85f09c7d94541 I 
needed to emulate a Boolean flag in Excel and used the Fujitsu COBOL 
extension which allows Binary (PIC 1(n)). The general reaction was 
raspberries (I didn't like it myself :-)) and I think we got round it in the 
end by using -1...


>
> If these points are worth making, could you pass them on reworded for
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> comp.lang.cobol.

I agree. I enjoyed posts from Dan Summers (who is a generally reasonable 
man) and even from Judson McClendon who was a bit more out there... both 
very capable COBOL guys. I still get the odd private mail from Daniel and we 
have been known to Skype at Xmas :-). Dan is  doing some really interesting 
stuff, more connected with C# than COBOL these days. I confess that some of 
his last mail was over my head :-)

As a pretty much confirmed atheist myself, I like it when I can find 
Christian people who are prepared to discuss things rationally, where we can 
agree to disagree and still be friends. It reinforces hope for the world... 
:-)


Pete

<a id="t-f7b2bd27d9"></a>
## Thread: [OT] My, How Things Have Changed — 15 msgs

### [OT] My, How Things Have Changed

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2010-11-03T00:08:39+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<iaq967$5hl$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```

I learned something that tickled my my mind and thought that others, even 
less well-schooled than I - if such a thing is possible! - might 
appreciate this treasure-in-a-pebble.

The concept of 'SQL injection' is not foreign to me but it existed only as 
that... a concept; when I code screens they're invoked by EXEC CICS and 
followed by a last-to-first check of fields for edit failures.  As anyone 
with a few decades' of experience might know name-checking (both for 
people and addresses) is its own Art.

I ran across the example of 'Little Bobby Tables' for the first time (the 
name appears in a UseNet posting of 2003 and the earliest 'explanation' of 
it I can find is http://xkcd.com/327/ (which appears to be from 2007)) and 
was amused, enlightened, stunned and horrified, all simultaneously.  That 
*anyone* would allow an interface which permitted user input to slip below 
the application interface and fall into (for lack of better terminology) 
the command-interpreter gave me Great Pause; my first response was 'how 
could such a thing ever pass a QA review?'...

... and the answer came back, out of the abyss, as it were, of 'They don't 
do those much any more.'  And in a way... they do and they don't, 
depending on who 'they' is.  I've seen websites that are, to my 
steam-powered way of thinking, a delight... the equivalent of a mechanic's 
manual for an automobile where one moves the cursor over an area and an 
expanded view comes up, and expansions within those views, and without 
remembering X1AB-7725-6A315-44817 one can order a replacement bracket, 
fixture, bit of trim or individual screw.

On the other hand... I can easily imagine a small school district (or even 
an individual school not open to general admission, called 'private' in 
the United States of America and 'public' in BritSpeak-land) where someone 
who knows a bit of computer-manipulation puts together a... something to 
keep track of people/stuff/events... and Someone Important glances over a 
shoulder or at a print-out and says 'That might be helpful if only we 
could... '... and it grows, organically, into a collection of patches and 
kludges like the Systems of Old did...

... but without the initial rigor required by the Systems of Old, with 
their Glass Houses and High Priests and folks who would actually approach 
the task with the discipline of people at least pretending to do Science.  
This is not to denigrate their inventiveness, creativity or 
problem-solving ability but just as a species changes to reflect its 
environment so might solutions to a problem - the same problem - be 
different when their formulators or audiences are The Homebrew Computer 
Society instead of The Association for Computing Machinery.

This and a (coin of small value) will get me (a minute container of a 
beverage)... but as goes the aphorism to which I passingly referred in the 
opening paragraph, 'Blessed is he who finds treasures in pebbles; he will 
always be surrounded by riches.'

DD
```

In reading the posting below and the cartoon that it pointed to I
became confused and worried.  Does this mean that a CICS transaction
with static SQL is vulnerable to SQL injection?  Does it mean that
once something gets on a database it could become SQL code at some
future point?  As someone who gave up trying to validate names because
of the variation (O'Henry for example), this has me concerned.  The
validation checking for this might be esoteric to say the least.  Is a
right parenthesis invalid in a person's name or a place name, for
example?  

Clark Morris

```
On Nov 3, 10:16 am, Clark F Morris <cfmpub...@ns.sympatico.ca> wrote:
> In reading the posting below and the cartoon that it pointed to I
> became confused and worried.  Does this mean that a CICS transaction
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> example?  


SQL injection is principally an issue with dynamically constructed SQL
queries that use in-line values for parameters.  Static SQL statements
are usually not vulnerable, nor are dynamic ones where all the values
are either pre-defined or come from variables outside the SQL
statement (“?” place holders or  “@” variables in stored procedures,
for example).

See:  http://www.owasp.org/index.php/SQL_Injection
```

>with static SQL is vulnerable to SQL injection?

To the best of my knowledge, Mr Morris, no.

>Does it mean that
>once something gets on a database it could become SQL code at some
>future point?

To the best of my knowledge, Mr Morris, that is the concept behind 'stored 
procedures', chunks of SQL that get stored in a dataset/table and then 
invoked.

>As someone who gave up trying to validate names because
>of the variation (O'Henry for example), this has me concerned.

It is good to know one's own limits, aye... although how one learns one's 
limits without exceeding them might be left for another lesson.

>The
>validation checking for this might be esoteric to say the least.  Is a
>right parenthesis invalid in a person's name or a place name, for
>example?  

I do not believe that the Little Bobby Tables scenario would appear in Ye 
Olde Style of coding, where CICS maps and COBOL work-areas are. for the 
most part, rather well delineated.  If one is working with a lower-level 
language and system then the borders might become fuzzier and the 
possibility for injection increases.

DD

And 3 or 4 basic and fundamental checks eliminate 99% of them.

In this day and age the only way an injection attack can work is by 
negligence on the part of a developer.

But if it worries you, get off SQL.

LINQ is an infintely better solution and injection attacks are "not 
applicable" if it is written properly. (User input is converted to 
parameters and cannot be part of the directly executed string.)

Pete.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: My, How Things Have Changed

- **From:** "robertwessel2@yahoo.com" <robertwessel2@yahoo.com>
- **Date:** 2010-11-03T16:49:36-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<441c50e0-a27d-4dcc-8969-c5a185005225@g25g2000yqn.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<iaq967$5hl$1@reader1.panix.com> <6ab29326-da36-4782-ac27-8c6fd0ffffd1@v16g2000yqn.googlegroups.com> <8je98cFnbeU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
On Nov 3, 6:23 pm, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
> Alistair Maclean wrote:
> > On Nov 3, 12:08 am, docdw...@panix.com () wrote:
…[69 more quoted lines elided]…
> parameters and cannot be part of the directly executed string.)


Whether LINQ is "infinitely better" is perhaps debatable, but that
solution to injection attacks is exactly the same one correctly
written SQL uses.  The syntax varies from language to language, and
the follow Java example is modified from the OWASP site:

// Unsafe
 String query = "SELECT account_balance FROM user_data WHERE user_name
= '" + custname + "'";
 ResultSet results = statement.executeQuery( query );

// Safe:
 String query = "SELECT account_balance FROM user_data WHERE user_name
= ? ";
 PreparedStatement pstmt = connection.prepareStatement( query );
 pstmt.setString( 1, custname);
 ResultSet results = pstmt.executeQuery( );

There are other solutions as well, but proper parameterization is
generally the best solution.
```

```
Alistair Maclean wrote:
> On Nov 5, 1:11 am, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[21 more quoted lines elided]…
> Does DB2 support LINQ? (he asked innocently)....

I've only used it with SQL Server, but it is designed for use with any data 
repository. I should think it is possible through ODBC but you would need to 
write the query in C# or call/invoke a Class written in C#, as LINQ is 
"Language INtegrated".

Let the man who invented it explain it: 
http://blogs.msdn.com/b/charlie/archive/2007/01/26/anders-hejlsberg-on-linq-and-functional-programming.aspx

(Click the "stream it" link on the page to see an excellent video.)

By the way, I'm not so stupid that I seriously think that all the mainframe 
sites using SQL COULD move to LINQ (without a great deal of effort) and some 
of this conversation was with tongue in cheek.

I DO believe that LINQ (and the functional programming that supports it) IS 
better than SQL for manipulating data, but at the moment it is largely 
academic. The syntax is worth investigating, but, currently you would need a 
free download of C# and Visual Studio in order to do so.

Probably some people who wish to teach themselves C# will do that anyway and 
it then becomes an option for them.

Pete.
```

- **Date:** 2010-11-03T04:09:53-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1e8ff9cb-1874-407e-b6dd-288bf7d80743@32g2000yqz.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<4cc8ed15$0$14832$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net> <8isgfvFpgjU1@mid.individual.net> <4ccc28f5$0$14815$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net>`

```
On 30 Okt., 15:17, Paul <paul-nospamatall.rauler...@mac.com> wrote:
> On 2010-10-28 00:37:01 -0500, Pete Dashwood said:
>
…[95 more quoted lines elided]…
> -Paul

oops, "historical data"

Paul, this is a typical issue within migration projects and it is
sometimes overlooked when data is kept in a non portable format.

When planning migration projects it is a good idea to assign some
extra time for converting whatever data is archived into a format that
can be migrated to the new target system.

I can recall an rfp where a couple of thousand cartridges where to be
taken into account, not easy to estimate what time it is going to
take.

Regards Hans

```
Hi:

First, the only time I would ever batch compile is if, for example,
a record format used by all (or most) programs were changed. On those
rare occasions when it is necessary, my DOS batch file does it in
a flash without intervention.

So, when I want to make a 'project' (I assume my POS systems are
'Projects'),
I just use the Wise Installation software to create an installation
EXE
where everything needed for the creation is in the same directory
(with no
sub-directories).  It takes about 7 seconds.

My complete installable 'project' is 2.5 meg.

I took the time to watch your video and I think it would qualify as
Theatre of the Absurd.

It seems to me that you are making mountains out of what should be
molehills.

Apparently, your molehills are not like my molehills.

Thanks

Tony Dilworth
```

```
foodman wrote:
> Hi:
>
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> a flash without intervention.

Good. How do you know it all worked?
>
> So, when I want to make a 'project' (I assume my POS systems are
> 'Projects'),

Assumptions are usually risky...

To be clear, when I started the thread I was intending the word "Project" to 
mean "Computer project files". These are files used by Fujitsu and Micro 
Focus (for example...) to allow the grouping of sources, objects, and 
resources so they can be easily managed via an IDE, usually with a GUI. 
Using a Project file enables you to manage your other "project-related" 
files more easily.

Collecting a bunch of sources and compiling them (outside of such an IDE), 
while it may loosely be considered to be a "Project" (in the same way that 
all the activities and resources required to build an office block can be 
considered a "Project"), is not specifically what I had in mind.

I think the link that was posted and the video on it make this pretty clear, 
but I can understand it appearing "absurd" to some people. (Probably the 
same ones to whom a technology they have never experienced is called "magic" 
or "Satanic"...)

> I just use the Wise Installation software to create an installation
> EXE
> where everything needed for the creation is in the same directory
> (with no
> sub-directories).  It takes about 7 seconds.

Sure. If you have a small application there is nothing wrong with doing 
that.

However, the thread is about PROJECTS. The link was about batch compiling 
Fujitsu COBOL Projects.


>
> My complete installable 'project' is 2.5 meg.

I think you'll find that is an application. A typical Project file is much 
smaller than that.
>
> I took the time to watch your video and I think it would qualify as
> Theatre of the Absurd.

Thank you for taking the time. Hopefully, your evaluation will encourage 
more people to view it.

>
> It seems to me that you are making mountains out of what should be
> molehills.
>

I'm happy to leave it to moles to decide what SHOULD be a molehill.

I feel pretty comfortable around mountains. We have a lot of them where I 
live. On the other hand, we don't have moles and the only time I have 
encountered them is during overseas visits. I feel pretty confident I can 
distinguish a mountain from a molehill and vice versa, but that isn't for me 
to say.

The feedback from people using the tool would indicate they don't see it as 
a mountain or a molehill; they just see it as "useful".

(People wishing to make up their own minds on this are invited to review the 
tool at: http://primacomputing.co.nz/PRIMAWebSite/BatchCompile.aspx )

> Apparently, your molehills are not like my molehills.
>

I fervently hope not.

> Thanks

You're welcome.

Pete.
```

- **References:** `<8intu7FmsqU1@mid.individual.net> <e3b535a2-dee6-4e41-8f52-0934072b068d@g25g2000yqn.googlegroups.com> <8jh67cF837U1@mid.individual.net>`

```
On Nov 5, 2:50 pm, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
> foodman wrote:
> > Hi:
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> Good. How do you know it all worked?

When using batch/shell scripts and/or make files it is quite easy to
see if they 'worked'. A simple grep at the end will produce a summary
of all the errors found in the .lst files.

For example with MicroFocus a 'grep Total.Messages *.LST' should show
all these lines to have 0.

It is also possible to get make to output a list of what needs to be
done without actually doing it (option -n) so this will show what
failed to produce its target.

Just build these into the script to create appropriate results files.


> > So, when I want to make a 'project' (I assume my POS systems are
> > 'Projects'),
…[35 more quoted lines elided]…
> smaller than that.

It is quite clear from your opening paragraph:

"""A few months back I posted here asking if anyone had some simple
code to
batch conpile Fujitsu Projects."""

 .. that a 'Project' includes the program code that is compiled to
produce the executables. This may well be several megabytes of various
files. It happens that there is a relatively small file that has a
list of what comprises the project and the relationships between these
parts.

One may say that a 'Project' is a work that has a result that is an
application.


> > I took the time to watch your video and I think it would qualify as
> > Theatre of the Absurd.
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> I'm happy to leave it to moles to decide what SHOULD be a molehill.

I have not found an IDE that I liked. It always seems to me that IDEs
were originally created because of the clumsiness of single-tasking MS-
DOS, and lack of tools like make. Turbo-Pascal for example built the
compiler and the editor into one program so that it was easy to switch
between these modes.

I have used multi-tasking/multi-user systems since the late 70s and
these had decent file managers that could jump into an editor of my
choice (which were  multi-file). A keystroke which switch to another
task window to kick off make which would run in the background while I
switched back to do other work (on 8086 systems compiles did take a
while).

Consequently I consider that while your solution is designed to suit a
specific need, it seems to me that it is a 'solution' to a problem
with GUIs to do a task that shouldn't be done with a GUI.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Dealing with Projects

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-11-08T12:21:52+13:00

```
Richard wrote:
> On Nov 5, 2:50 pm, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>> Good. How do you know it all worked?

The question was to Tony.

I wanted to know how HE knows it all worked.
>
> When using batch/shell scripts and/or make files it is quite easy to
> see if they 'worked'. A simple grep at the end will produce a summary
> of all the errors found in the .lst files.

Grep is not available on Windows without a specific download of third party 
software which most Windows users find no need for. Global replacement edits 
can be done in many other ways.
>
> For example with MicroFocus a 'grep Total.Messages *.LST' should show
> all these lines to have 0.

A batch compile can return zero and still have failed. (The compiler ran OK, 
it just didn't compile error free.) It depends on how it is invoked and 
whether shell is used.
>
> It is also possible to get make to output a list of what needs to be
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> Just build these into the script to create appropriate results files.

Nothing wrong with what you are suggesting but it is only one way and not a 
Windows friendly way. The Windows system is designed for Graphic User 
Interface, using Windows OS via "windows" on screen. The majority of Windows 
users enjoy the simplicity of a point-and-click interface and don't want the 
complexity of a CLI. GUI interfaces are intuitive; CLIs require learning 
esoteric commands and understanding of what goes on under the covers. Guess 
which one has swept the world?

There should be no need to use CLI (although you can if you want to, of 
course).
>
>
…[44 more quoted lines elided]…
> batch conpile Fujitsu Projects."""

NOT  'a bunch of COBOL source code' although that would certanly be part of 
the project.

>
>  .. that a 'Project' includes the program code that is compiled to
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> application.

And one would be right. But one could say many things and they would all be 
right.
>
>
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> switch between these modes.

There are probably many people who feel the same, just as there are others 
who LOVE their IDE. (I'm a great fan of Visual Studio, not because I get 
emotional about software, just because it has saved me many hous of tiresome 
work. I think of the years of my life spent working on ISPF screens and I 
smile about it. When they first became available we thought they were 
fantastic; to be able to back up a cursor and change a typed line was a long 
way ahead of punching a new card. Life (and computer technology) moves on. 
Pointing and clicking, dragging and dropping to build components and 
solutions is just a quantum level above using a CLI, in my opinion. I like 
my IDE and have no iontention of going back to previous solutions.)

>
> I have used multi-tasking/multi-user systems since the late 70s and
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> with GUIs to do a task that shouldn't be done with a GUI.

I take your point and accept that what you describe works very well for you.

As for the tool addressing a problem that doesn't exist, the people who use 
it would strongly disagree. I have taken to using it myself and it 
definitely helps to have things centralised. Remember, this tool doesn't 
JUST do batch compilation, it also allows individual projects (which you are 
currently interested in) to be  popped up and worked on without having to 
browse directory hierarchies, and it allows multiple projects to be worked 
on and compared easily, then rebuilt/compiled with a mouse click.

I am not suggesting that this is the ONLY way to deal with Fujitsu projects; 
I am suggesting that, for people using Windows, it is a good way.

When I suggested here some time back (2008) that having a tool to analyse 
COBOL data structures might be useful, the following exchange ensued:

==============  begin quote from CLC archives =========================

On Aug 30, 5:20 pm, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
> "Richard" <rip...@azonic.co.nz> wrote in message
>
…[32 more quoted lines elided]…
> could be developing a record layout that has never been compiled...)

How hard would it be to write a couple of lines around a record layout
so that the compiler will process it ?

Some people have no imagination.
===================  End quoted text ======================

There is nothing "wrong" with what you said but, despite your barbed final 
comment aimed at me, it is you who was lacking imagination.

The tool was produced, and used as an exercise to demonstrate the ease with 
which standard COBOL can become Object Oriented. It analyses partial or full 
record layouts (which compilers generally don't) and can accept input from 
the system clipboard (which compilers generally don't). Users can select 
source they are looking at or working on with a mouse, copy it to the 
clipboard with the standard Ctrl/C they all know and love and then have it 
analysed instantly on screen. No CLI required.

(http://primacomputing.co.nz/cobol21/newcobdata.aspx)

Despite your dismissal as unnecessary and unimaginative,  and easily 
replaceable by a few lines of script, 300 people have downloaded and use 
this tool.(When I'm working with COBOL I have it sitting on my taskbar and 
find it useful. One client who downloaded it as part of a data migration, 
said it was fundamental to helping his programmers (who were not COBOL guys) 
understand and use COBOL data. Another uses it at the heart of a Relational 
database to serve up data from a COBOL legacy to VB front ends.  It has been 
used in ways and for purposes which neither Robert nor myself could have 
imagined at the time we developed it.)

The 300 people are Windows users.

They interact with their computer via a window and a mouse.

They LIKE to do that; many (most?) of them have no idea about using scripts 
and don't want any.

The point I am making here is that there are many ways to work and many 
different environments to work in.

You use an environment that ISN'T Windows and you have the skills and 
background to master it. It supports a GUI just as Windows does but you 
personally feel there are some things which should NOT be done with a GUI 
(like running batch compiles and builds...) Fair enough. That's your 
opinion. (I'd like to see EVERYTHING run through a point and click 
interface, but that is just my opinion...)

What you do isn't wrong and your opinions are not wrong either. But neither 
are they true for peope who DON'T work in your environment.

Telling a Windows user to run "grep" is like telling a Unix user to open 
wordpad. Of course people can download grep for windows but they don't need 
to. It is just one way to do things.

It isn't "wrong" but it isn't helpful either.

Here is a verbatim quote from a Windows user who uses the new Projects tool:

====================  begin quote ===============================

Hi Pete,

I really like the new enhancements.

Having the projects listed in their name order, makes it easier to exclude 
some of our backup projects (names prefixed with 'Copy').  I also found that 
we do have a .ppj & a .prj with the same name, and as you said the tool 
handles them just fine with the consolidated report.

I really appreciate the more button,  I can now remove all projects that I 
have excluded and see only  the ones that I want to compile and then when 
some of them failed I can now easily manipulate the list to have only  the 
ones I need to fix.  (Now I do not need to remove the backup projects to a 
different folder and this is helpful).

I ran the tool to compile all the projects for xxxxxxxxxx, it compiled 114 
projects in just under two hours.
And I like the fact that I can run the batch compile, leave it in the 
background to work on other things and still be able to check the progress 
every now and then as the GUI  no longer freezes.

Thanks Pete - we will definitely enjoy the tool.

============================ end quote 
=======================================

While Foodman may consider it absurd, and you may consider this should be 
done through CLI, there are other people who don't see things that way.

I'm one of them.

Pete.
```

You may find that 'Windows NT Resource Kit' and 'Windows Services for

> which most Windows users find no need for. Global replacement edits
> can be done in many other ways.

They may find 'no need' mainly because they can only cope with GUI
point-and-grunt. For example you conflate grep reports with "global
replacement edits" which implies all the usual GUI clicking around
until you reach the required information while a grep buried in a
script could present the results automatically and directly.


> > For example with MicroFocus a 'grep Total.Messages *.LST' should show
> > all these lines to have 0.
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> whether shell is used.

Which is why I presented one of the available easy solutions (below).

> > It is also possible to get make to output a list of what needs to be
> > done without actually doing it (option -n) so this will show what
> > failed to produce its target.
>
> > Just build these into the script to create appropriate results files.


> Nothing wrong with what you are suggesting but it is only one way and not a
> Windows friendly way. The Windows system is designed for Graphic User
> Interface, using Windows OS via "windows" on screen.

Why is it that you think that a script is incompatible with a 'window
on screen' ? Scripts can have a 'short cut' desktop icon, or be in the
system menu, or linked from most IDEs or editors and can present
information in a window (eg into notepad).

> The majority of Windows
> users enjoy the simplicity of a point-and-click interface and don't want the
> complexity of a CLI. GUI interfaces are intuitive; CLIs require learning
> esoteric commands and understanding of what goes on under the covers. Guess
> which one has swept the world?

And underneath all that is text files that are written by being keyed
into a text editor and compiled to produce programs. A script is just
another text file that produces results, which may indeed be in a GUI
window.

> There should be no need to use CLI (although you can if you want to, of
> course).

You have been fully sucked into the Microsoft 'CLIs are too hard for
your brain' mentality. Scripts do not need to be executed in a DOS box
by typing into the C:\> prompt. Scripts and commands are just another
programming language to solve problems with.

Far too often I see 'really easy to use' click-about user interfaces
for tasks that should not need any actual user interface at all. But
then much of my work involves automatic systems that collect
files,messages, emails, webpages, process them and send the results to
another system with no intervention at all.


> >>> So, when I want to make a 'project' (I assume my POS systems are
> >>> 'Projects'),
…[87 more quoted lines elided]…
>

It seems to me that you went very late, directly from ISPF like
systems to VS without any intermediate steps. This may have led you to
believe that systems are either DOS-like type-in-every-command line
parameter, or GUI click-around IDEs.

You may be surprised to find that scripts can be plugged into many
editors and/or IDEs to present information as the user requires it.

No, I don't type in the grep command or the make command with its
various parameters every time I want to compile and find what worked
and what didn't.  These are in scripts that do it for me, as
background tasks, and present the results that I need.


> > I have used multi-tasking/multi-user systems since the late 70s and

_Topics: [`Object-oriented COBOL`](topics.md#oo)_

### Phase 1 - OO Rosetta Bottles of Beer

- **From:** James Gavan <jgavan@shaw.ca>
- **Date:** 2010-11-07T12:38:11-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<FeDBo.18820$3f.1700@newsfe12.iad>`

```
Well I'm there about 99.9%. What really bugged me and held me up was to 
do the following. Bearing in mind Alistair's observation (complaint), it 
is a drag to go through a screen display. I arrived at four options :-

        Rosetta - NINETY-NINE BOTTLES

  (1) Display results on Screen
  (2) Write to Text File - Notepad Edit
  (3) Write to Text File - MS Word Edit
  (4) Show results in a GUI Listbox

      Enter choice : -

The one that held me up - dear ole Microsoft's Word with all the jazz 
needed to get at it as an OLE !!!!  It was in another project - Common 
Dialogs that I initially came up against the problem. But I thought I 
had solved it. Meanwhile I changed machines, and can't be sure what 
happened. We've all used the phrase "Well it used to work and I haven't 
changed anything....." Yes - it's a question of triggering a memory of 
what we *actually* did do.

To cut a long story short M/F had a demo - a Procedural example program 
CREATEP (Create Process) and through it they call Notepad to open an 
existing document. Works like a dream - and uses some three API Calls.

Not to digress at this stage between the simplicity of the API approach 
and getting an OLE version of MS Word to STAY ON THE DAMNED SCREEN, that 
is, pause and let you view what they have done, before it automatically 
quits, I've adapted # 2 above (which is the CreateP) to do exactly that 
for # 3 above, MS Word. I'm not advocatng APIs as a solution, but it 
works in this case. While browsing through my computer I came across an 
example from the young feisty Kellie Fitton, (from California), using 
APIs - remember her ? It works fine, but all that coding for APIs - 
hardly productive in the modern world.

More later on APIs and MS Word to see if we can get it working. Will be 
posted in a separate thread..

The following is no candidate for Rosetta, it goes way beyond the 
'cutsie' snippets of program code provided for most languages. (We will 
exclude Richard's Iteration Program from that comment). This is the 
heart of the topic in my version, the logic for the count.

This Bottles of Beer is a good topic for M/F users to show what can be 
done with OO - so I'll post a zipfile to the Micro Focus Forum. Even 
non-M/F users can access that site as 'Guests'. I'll let you know when 
done and how to get a download, if you are interested. I'll call that 
message 'Phase 2 - Bottles of Beer'

I hope it's understood this will only work with M/F compilers - I've 
used every trick in the book "exclude red tape" to reduce the coding.
I can't be certain, but I'm guessing it may work as far back as M/F's 
VISOC; I know my coding works with V 5.0, (I sent somebody in Brazil a 
separate early zipfile on 'TestDialogs') So if you do have a copy of the 
various compilers .....???

I did post a copy of this to CLC with an zip attachment, containing a 
Systems Flowchart and screenshots of the the displays from the four 
options. Didn't appear in CLC and you don't even get a message back 
saying 'your message was undelivered'.

So for the moment a Mickey Mouse version of the flowchart so that you 
can see where BottleCount below fits into the scenario.

**********************************************************

1. Trigger-Bottles
-------------------
intiates the Project &
first call to Win GUIAPIs

2. Driver-Bottles-App
----------------------------
Invokes (3) Mycollections to -------> 3.\copylib\MyCollections
create two collections                 ------------------------
(a) Text-Collection
(b) Object-Collection.

Passes these two collections -------> 4. Bottlecount (below)
to (4) BottleCount where elements      -----------------------
are added to the Collections

(5). If your choice was #1 - uses a
Callback to display on DOS Screen
from the Text-Collection

For Choices 2 and 3 uses a
Callback to write to (6) LineSeq
.
------------------------------------> 6. \Copylib\FileLineSeq
.                                     -----------------------
.                                     writes to diskfile
.                                     BottleCount.txt
.
.                                     7. \Copylib\FileErrors
.                                     ----------------------
.                                     File Status Errors
---------> 9. MyCreateP
.         -------------               8. \Coplib\MyMessages
.         Accesses disk to open       ----------------------
.         BottleCount.txt             invokes M/F messagebox.
.         in NotePad or MsWord
.
---------> 10.Dialog-Bottles
.          -----------------
.          (GUI parameters)
.
.--------> 11. MyDialog-Listbox-------> 12. \Copylib\MyDialog
           --------------------         ---------------------
           Sub-Class inheriting         Displays Object Collection
           from (12) MyDialog.          in a Dialog with a Listbox
           Has ONE method to override   and just an 'Exit' button
           the Listbox method in
           MyDialog - so that it
           doesn't need a Window event
           for the Listbox


******************************************************************


Here's the source of BottleCount

Jimmy, Calgary AB

APART FROM THE START METHOD "Main", all other methods are listed 
ALPHABETICALLY :-


  *>-----------------------BottleCount.cbl ------------------------
$set ooctrl(-w)

  *> Above Directive allows N/E V 3.1 to use 'Working-Storage'
  *> within methods

  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  *> OO COBOL - Micro Focus Net Express V3.1 and Wndows XP -
  *>
  *> Author : jgavan@shaw.ca     Date Revised : 2010 Oct 28
  *>
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  *>
  Class-id.           BottleCount inherits from Base.

  Class-Control.

          *> M/F Support classes :
          CharacterArray          is class "chararry"

          *> Your classes :
          BottleCount             is class "bottlecount"
          .

  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  FACTORY.
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
  copy "BottlesChoice.cpy".

  78 ML               value 10.   *> Message Length
  78 SC               value 22.   *> Change the value of this and
                                  *> re-compile if you want to
                                  *> whizz through the display

  78 TR               value 80.   *> Max-Length of Text-Result and
                                  *> Lnk-Element
  78 Tilde            value "~".

  01 charx                        pic x.
  01 Current-NumberName           pic x(15).
  01 Next-NumberName              pic x(15).
  01 Kounter-1                    pic 9(02).
  01 Text-Result                  pic x(TR).

  *> Literal Tables : Initially I tried placing these in the method
  *> they appeared to be solely relevant to i.e., "GetFiveLines".
  *> Unfortunately the indexing in the tables is used elsewhere.

  01  Digits-Table.
      05   pic x(ML) value "One~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Two~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Three~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Four~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Five~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Six~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Seven~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Eight~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Nine~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Ten~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Eleven~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Twelve~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Thirteen~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Fourteen~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Fifteen~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Sixteen~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Seventeen~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Eighteen~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Nineteen~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "~".

  01  Filler redefines Digits-Table.
      05 Digits  pic x(ML) occurs 20
                indexed by Digits-Idx.

  01  Tens-Table.
      05   pic x(ML) value "~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Twenty~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Thirty~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Forty~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Fifty~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Sixty~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Seventy~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Eighty~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "Ninety~".
      05   pic x(ML) value "~".

  01  filler redefines Tens-Table.
      05 Tens pic x(ML) occurs 10
              indexed by Tens-Idx.

  *>-------Object References.

  01 os-ObjectCollection       object reference value null.
  01 os-TextCollection         object reference value null.

  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "Main".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  Linkage section.
  01 lnk-Choice                      pic x(4) comp-5.
  01 lnk-ObjectCollection            object reference.
  01 lnk-TextCollection              object reference.

  Procedure Division
      using Lnk-Choice, Lnk-ObjectCollection, Lnk-TextCollection.

  move lnk-Choice          to BottlesChoice
  set  os-ObjectCollection to lnk-ObjectCollection
  set  os-TextCollection   to lnk-TextCollection
  move 99                  to Kounter-1
  invoke self "DecrementCount"

  *> Having finished with the method "DecrementCount", this class
  *> returns to BottleDriver where the results are displayed
  *> according to user's choice.

  End Method "Main".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "AddToList".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  01 RecordLength                 pic x(4) comp-5 value TR.
  01 ls-Object                    object reference.

  if    DisplayOnScreen
        invoke os-TextCollection "add" using Text-Result

  else  invoke CharacterArray "withLengthValue"
               using RecordLength, Text-Result
               returning ls-object
        invoke os-ObjectCollection "add" using ls-object
  end-invoke

  *> The two collectons above were created 'empty' from class
  *> Driver-Bottles-App. This class adds elements to either
  *> collection, but the updated Collections are *** NOT ***
  *> returned through Linkage to Driver-Bottles-App.

  *> With a 'common' object reference, shared with this Class,
  *> Driver-Bottles-App knows how many Elements this class has
  *> added and the properties associated with those elements.

  End Method "AddToList".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "DecrementCount".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------

  *> This is a RECURSIVE METHOD - i.e. the method re-invokes itself

  01 Subtractor                        pic 9.

  move zeroes to Subtractor
  invoke self "GetNumberName" using Subtractor
              returning Current-NumberName

  move 1 to Subtractor
  invoke self "GetNumberName" using Subtractor
              returning Next-NumberName

  invoke self "GetFiveLines"

  compute Kounter-1 = Kounter-1 - 1

  if    Kounter-1 <> zero
        invoke self "DecrementCount"
  End-if.

  End Method "DecrementCount".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "GetFiveLines".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  78 TL                value 35.
  78 MX                value 6.
  01 Text-Table.
   05 pic x(TL) value " Bottles of Beer~".                  *> 1
   05 pic x(TL) value " on the Wall .....~".                *> 2
   05 pic x(TL) value "Take one down and pass it around ".  *> 3
   05 pic x(TL) value "Only one Bottle left~".              *> 4
   05 pic x(TL) value "No more Beer left".                  *> 5
   05 pic x(TL) value "Please go get some more beer".       *> 6

  01 Filler
     redefines Text-Table.
     05 Temp-Text  occurs MX pic x(TL).

  01 LineNumber                       pic x(4) comp-5.

  *> Sample output specified by Rosetta :

  *> Line 1 - Ninety-Nine Bottles of Beer on the Wall .....
  *> Line 2 - Ninety-Nine Bottles of Beer
  *> Line 3 - Take one down and pass it around
  *> Line 4 - Ninety-Eight Bottles of Beer on the Wall .....
  *> Line 5 - spaces


  PERFORM varying LineNumber from 1 by 1 until LineNumber > 4

       Initialize Text-Result

       Evaluate true also true

       *>---------------------------------
       *> TABLE A : LineNumber = 1
       *>---------------------------------
       *> Kounter-1 > 2          y
       *> Kounter-1 = 2          -  y
       *> Kounter-1 = 1          -  -  y
       *>---------------------------------
       *> 1 - Plural             1  1  -
       *> 2 - On the Wall        2  2  2
       *> 3 - Take down          -  -  -
       *> 4 - Only one           -  -  4
       *> 5 - No More            -  -  -
       *> 6 - Go get             -  -  -
       *>---------------------------------

         when LineNumber = 1 also Kounter-1 > 2
         when LineNumber = 1 also Kounter-1 = 2

              string Current-NumberName delimited by Tilde
                     Temp-Text(1)       delimited by Tilde
                     Temp-Text(2)       delimited by Tilde
                     into Text-Result
              end-string
              invoke self "AddToList"

         when LineNumber = 1 also Kounter-1 = 1

              string Current-NumberName delimited by Tilde
                     Temp-Text(4)       delimited by Tilde
                     Temp-Text(2)       delimited by Tilde
                     into Text-Result
              end-string
              invoke self "AddToList"

       *>---------------------------------
       *> TABLE B : LineNumber = 2
       *>---------------------------------
       *> Kounter-1 > 2          y
       *> Kounter-1 = 2          -  y
       *> Kounter-1 = 1          -  -  y
       *>---------------------------------
       *> 1 - Plural             1  1  -
       *> 2 - On the Wall        -  -  -
       *> 3 - Take down          -  -  -
       *> 4 - Only one           -  -  4
       *> 5 - No More            -  -  -
       *> 6 - Go get             -  -  -
       *>---------------------------------

         when LineNumber = 2 also Kounter-1 > 2
         when LineNumber = 2 also Kounter-1 = 2

              string Current-NumberName delimited by Tilde
                     Temp-Text(1)       delimited by Tilde
                     into Text-Result
              end-string
              invoke self "AddToList"

         when LineNumber = 2 also Kounter-1 = 1

              string Current-NumberName delimited by Tilde
                     Temp-Text(4)       delimited by Tilde
                     into Text-Result
              end-string
              invoke self "AddToList"

       *>---------------------------------
       *> TABLE C : LineNumber = 3
       *>---------------------------------
       *> Kounter-1 > 2          y
       *> Kounter-1 = 2          -  y
       *> Kounter-1 = 1          -  -  y
       *>---------------------------------
       *> 1 - Plural             -  -  -
       *> 2 - On the Wall        -  -  -
       *> 3 - Take down          3  3  3
       *> 4 - Only one           -  -  -
       *> 5 - No More            -  -  -
       *> 6 - Go get             -  -  -
       *>---------------------------------

         when LineNumber = 3 also any

              move Temp-Text(3) to Text-Result
              invoke self "AddToList"

       *>---------------------------------
       *> TABLE D : LineNumber = 4
       *>---------------------------------
       *> Kounter-1 > 2          y
       *> Kounter-1 = 2          -  y
       *> Kounter-1 = 1          -  -  y
       *>---------------------------------
       *> 1 - Plural             1  -  -
       *> 2 - On the Wall        2  -  -
       *> 3 - Take down          -  -  -
       *> 4 - Only one           -  4  -
       *> 5 - No More            -  -  5
       *> 6 - Go get             -  -  6
       *>---------------------------------

         when LineNumber = 4 also Kounter-1 > 2

              string Next-NumberName    delimited by Tilde
                     Temp-Text(1)       delimited by Tilde
                     Temp-Text(2)       delimited by Tilde
                     into Text-Result
              end-string
              invoke self "AddToList"

              move spaces to Text-Result
              invoke self "AddToList"

         when LineNumber = 4 also Kounter-1 = 2

              string Temp-Text(4) delimited by Tilde
                     into Text-Result
              invoke self "AddToList"

              move spaces to Text-Result
              invoke self "AddToList"

         when LineNumber = 4 also Kounter-1 = 1

              move Temp-Text(5) to Text-Result
              invoke self "AddToList"
              move Temp-Text(6) to Text-Result
              invoke self "AddToList"

       End-Evaluate
  END-PERFORM

  End Method "GetFiveLines".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "GetNumberName".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  78 HyphenTilde              value "-~".

  01 Descrip-1                pic x(10).
  01 Separator                pic x(02).
  01 Descrip-2                pic x(10).

  01 Kounter-2                pic 9(02).
  01 Kounter-3
      redefines Kounter-2.
     10 K-Tens                pic 9.
     10 K-Digits              pic 9.

  Linkage Section.
  01 lnk-Subtractor                   pic 9.
  01 lnk-NumberName                   pic x(15).

  Procedure Division using     lnk-Subtractor
                    returning lnk-NumberName.

  if      lnk-Subtractor = zeroes
          compute Kounter-2 = Kounter-1

  else    compute Kounter-2 = Kounter-1 - 1
  end-if

  *> Initialize the three fields :
  move Tilde       to Descrip-1, Descrip-2
  move HyphenTilde to Separator

  if    K-Tens <> zeroes
        set Tens-Idx to K-Tens
  end-if

  Evaluate true

      when Kounter-2 = zeroes
      when Kounter-2 = 1
           move Tilde to Separator

      when Kounter-2 < 20
           set  Digits-Idx to Kounter-2
           Move Tilde to Descrip-1, Separator
           move Digits (Digits-Idx) to Descrip-2

      when other
           move Tens (Tens-idx) to Descrip-1

           if   K-Digits <> zero
                set Digits-Idx to K-Digits
                move Digits (Digits-Idx) to Descrip-2

           else move Tilde to Separator, Descrip-2
           end-if
  End-Evaluate

  String Descrip-1 delimited by Tilde
         Separator delimited by Tilde
         Descrip-2 delimited by Tilde
         Tilde
         into lnk-NumberName
  end-string

  End Method "GetNumberName".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  END FACTORY.
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  *>OBJECT.           OBJECT/iNSTANCE not used with Abstract/
  *>END OBJECT.       Singleton classes
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------

  END CLASS BottleCount.
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
```

On Mon, 08 Nov 2010 17:47:46 +0100, Fritz Wuehler
<fritz@spamexpire-201011.rodent.frell.theremailer.net> wrote:

>James Gavan <jgavan@shaw.ca> wrote:
>
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>problems! Just use C++ if you need it so badly. Otherwise, be a man!

That code was an exercise (you don't think beer inventory was a
business application??).   Playing around like that can improve our
understanding of OO CoBOL.   

The normal situation for writing OO-CoBOL isn't with new applications
- especially relatively simple new applications.   OO-CoBOL is most
often used to convert existing CoBOL to work in an OO environment.
Practicing one's OO-CoBOL skills can assist in evaluating the costs
and benefits of converting CoBOL vs replacing it.
```

TOP POST - nothing more below.

Thanks for posting this, Jimmy.

I like the recursive COBOL method and think it is a good approach.

Overall, the code looks a bit intimidating and I'm not sure that some of the 
repeated WHERE tests couldn't be avoided.

It seems to me there are COPYed members that are not included, but as I 
don't have a Micro Focus environment I couldn't try compiling the code.

You will have seen some of the comments this has evinced.

I think those concerns are worth addressing, so have started another thread 
about the relevance of OO COBOL.

Cheers,

Pete.

On 11/8/2010 4:57 PM, Pete Dashwood wrote:
> TOP POST - nothing more below.
>
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> You will have seen some of the comments this has evinced.

Yes, the first from our friend in Oz; the "Author' wasn't offended and 
in fact had a bloody good laugh. The only words of advice I can give to 
him are, "Stick with Java, cobber and go throw another 'roo on the barbie'".
>
> I think those concerns are worth addressing, so have started another thread
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> Pete.

Agreed, it does seem like there are lots of EVALUATEs - which might 
appear unnecessary. But as Howard observed, it *IS* a tutorial approach, 
so although some might suggest you don't need the Decision Tables to 
show what's going on, anybody thinking of taking advantage can adjust 
the code to what they want it to be. Richard once mentioned you could go 
from Decision Tables to generating the checking code - care to give me a 
suggestion Richard to improve on what I've shown ?

Pete,  one observation on the code you wrote - in your program, which 
admittedly was a quick revamp of the effort from Bruce; you used 'String 
with Spaces'. OK, so some joker says, now extend the puzzle starting at 
200 and working you way down. Now we are back to 'South Pacific' - 
what's the easy way to handle the song :-

"One hundred and one pounds of fun, That's my little Honey Bun...." - 
the Tilde can be a very useful separator/joiner.

I was hoping you at least would have a copy of Net Express - doesn't 
matter if it is an old one; I think my code will fit.

The complete code I will be packaging will have copyfiles included, with 
the exception of the following, which I'm guessing I shouldn't 
distribute - copy files from Micro Focus. These are things like :-

p2cevent.cpy - GUI events - primarily Level 88s or Level 78s and Hex 
values for events etc. Accepting that they are there, you don't have the 
complete story, but I think something like 98% will be understood.
And if you do have a copy of Net Express these copyfiles are 
automatically added to your project as soon as you include them in one 
single source program.

Similarly I have heavily commented the features I have used - such as 
Collections, Callbacks - the first some will be familiar with, but I'm 
guessing Callbacks might be a bummer to some.

Here's a conundrum - where others may wish to join in. My MS Word 
document describing intent, included source and copyfiles, flowchart and 
4 sceenshots, etc... is all but done.

I've been debating which font. The very, very rare occasion I've used 
Word to send a private letter, my preference has been Times New Roman.
Anybody making suggestions bear in mind - people like Bill Klein have 
sight disabilities, so anything chosen has to be a compromise as to what 
is an easy read for most, but also takes into account people like Bill.

I like Times New Roman, but I think it's a bit too stylish for 
documentation. Perhaps one of the Arials with point 12 or 14 for text, 
and 16 for Para-Headers and I also think it should be BOLD for 
readability. Any takers ?

Another query with MS WORD - I went through my already written text, 
changing fonts and their properties to get a visual impression. Strange 
thing is I found that having made some changes, there was too much 
"depth" between lines. Suppose I initially set up a paragraph as Point 
14, if then doing a 'block replacement' by highlighting - changing to 
Point 12 - the result is I still see the same depth for Point 14. Is 
there some Word limitation, that once you have written something, you 
have to delete it if you have played around using the Point feature, and 
have to rewrite that text ?

Jimmy

On 11/8/2010 7:04 PM, Pete Dashwood wrote:
> James Gavan wrote:
>> On 11/8/2010 4:57 PM, Pete Dashwood wrote:
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>>> I like the recursive COBOL method and think it is a good approach.

To be perfectly truthful I've only ever used a recursive method ONCE 
before. Background on that was the old (deceased corrosion testing 
system). Not unusual for Klaus (died in March) to whistle between two 
oil/gas plants in the same area, because of an urgent request by the 
local manager. So that tended to throw him when he got back to Plant A 
from Plant B. "Which was the last Vessel I was working on, and which 
particular item ( = pipe) ?". "Be nice if you could give me some sort of 
reminder".

So I hit on the idea of using a Treeview of the Plant : Level 0 - Plant,
Level 2 - Vessel, Level 3 - Item etc... To simplify the testing I used a 
Treeview of Cheeses : Level 0 - Cheeses, Level 1 - Continent, Level 2 - 
Country, Level 3 - the actual cheese names. Each element in the Treeview 
had an icon, (could just as easily have been a checkbox). Starting out 
from scratch (a particular Inspection Date in corrosion) all icons were 
Red (unactioned). As you change something for a Cheese it was necessary 
to change the icon colour to Green. That required an override method to 
the normal GUI reaction. (My first intro to overriding and provided for 
me by David Sands of Micro Focus - absolutely dead easy when you have an 
example).

The logic was Cheeses - change to Green individually but you could only 
change the Country icon when all cheeses for that country showed Green. 
Similarly you could only change the Continent icon to Green when all 
countries in that group were Green. And finally the Root Level is only 
Green when all subordinates show Green.

I think that particular problem did lend itself nicely to a recursive 
method. (Well I suppose I could have written perform until 
NoMoreToBeActioned). To be frank for Bottles of Beer, I consider the 
recursive method to be a bit gimmicky, (the technique is just used, 
'because it is available'). Could just as easily have been a PERFORM the 
Decrement method varying count from 99 until count = zero. Regardless of 
which OO COBOL compiler we are talking about - I'm sure their mechanisms 
are fairly close for this. Either PERFORM or doing the RECURSIVE 'call' 
- the method we are 'exiting' is still in memory and I'd bet each 
compiler checks if it is wanted again before 'throwing the method away'. 
As they all probably have some cache technique for current methods, it's 
unlikely it wont be available immediately for re-use.

>>>
>>> Overall, the code looks a bit intimidating and I'm not sure that
>>> some of the repeated WHERE tests couldn't be avoided.

Well for the uninitiated - I will be adding the following at the start 
of each source :-

*>---------------------------------------------------------------
*> OO COBOL - Micro Focus Net Express V3.1 and Windows XP -
*>
*> Author : jgavan@shaw.ca     Date Revised : 2010 Nov 03
*>
*> The DIRECTIVE above :- $set ooctrl(-w)
*>
*> allows N/E V 3.1 to use 'Working-Storage' within methods
*>
*> "Ignore red tape" - Method format.
*>
*> From the directive above, the heading "Working-Storage Section"
*> is assumed within methods, by the compiler. Local-Storage
*> Section is superfluous.
*>
*> The only time you require 'Procedure Division......' in a
*> method is when it is associated with a Linkage-Section where
*> the syntax then reads as one of the three options:-
*>
*>      Procedure Division using xxxxx
*>      Procedure Division returning yyyyy
*>      Procedure Division using xxxxx returning yyyyy
*>
*>---------------------------------------------------------------


> I noted (and was surprised) you said you had problems using the OLE
> Automation server and reverted to the API instead. It should be a simple
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> how hard can it be :-)?)

As regards MS Word I could spend many unproductive hours messing around 
with it - holding me up releasing the code for 99-Bottles - so I'll take 
another look later. Meanwhile I'll go with the MyCreateP (API Create 
Process) which automatically opens Notepad or Word and close them as 
they see fit.

Whether or not it has always been the case, but one of the senior people 
from Bill's generation wrote a white paper where one suggestion was 
finalize the object for MsWord, (i.e. disconnect COBOL from the OLE) and 
leave Word there just hanging. Don't like the idea, but it implies the 
OLE routines are not clear cut. (Just google on Create Process, 
Terminate Process associated with APIs and Word/Excel - see all the crap 
you get !). And that's one of the major bitches I have with MS ! They 
have reams of articles/KBs on similar/parallel topics. Somebody needs to 
sit down and revamp their library. I'm not referring to COBOLERs only - 
people in EVERY language have the same problems with MS.

Take the following. Somebody in the M/F Forum asked, "Can I enlarge the 
Open Dialog ?". I know what he was after - increase the dimensions and 
he can view more files. I got back to him saying I hadn't found that 
that could be done. As I was into the Common Dialogs project at the time 
I gave it a try. I changed the x, y co-ordinates from their default to a 
value of say 12 - yes it displayed moved down and across the parent 
window the 12 value, but totally ignored my values for width) and 
h(eight). Well that concluded it can't be done.

Quite by accident, going through the above crap I came across a KB 
Article. "You can't change w or h in Windows XP - but if you have 
Windows Vista, 7 etc... voila !"  Doesn't it make sense to consolidate 
into one article with a proviso about exceptions per version of the OS ? 
The hours you can waste on this. (Don't tell me about your one-liner 
methods in .Net - I'm still using XP).

(As an after-thought, but it is re-inventing the wheel, you could design 
your own version of Open Dialog, (using a SortedCollection) with a 
scrolled list of files. You could be more expansive showing the file 
extension and even Date I would suggest).

To be fair - and I can't recall exactly what I was looking at, but 
dealing with Common Dialog - Open Files, I came across an example in 
BASIC (not using the VB wizard routines - which are only useful if you 
are using VB), and I think it was associated with .Net, spelling out how 
you could customize the Open File Dialog; couldn't have been any more 
clear if they tried ! I'm referring to the Droplist of file types you 
can open. When testing, I got frustrated when a set sequence popped up, 
say the first line was *.txt which I would use for Notepad; had to 
scroll down to get *.doc for Word. To hell with it - from the Driver for 
my project Common Dialogs I allow you to select from a menu - use Open 
Dialog (a) for *.txt and (b) for *.doc and just re-arrange (a) or (b) as 
the first line in the OrderedCollection displayed in the Open File 
Dialog.

Jimmy
