```
On 11/9/2010 7:21 PM, Richard wrote:
> On Nov 10, 1:19 pm, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz>  wrote:
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
>
My reference is to these last two sentences.

>> At least in the Fujitsu environment (I'm not sure about other OO COBOL
>> environments) it is possible for non-OO COBOL code to invoke OO COBOL
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> modules that CALL the one so that they now INVOKE it.

# 1 - sure you can in M/F too. Excluding the totally OO-ish demos for : -

- Phone (a list of Employees and info on them, in a Listbox)
- Bank (Yes the ubiquitous use of Bank Accounts)

Their other demos, including those you can download from their Homepage 
are stand-alone projects for the most part. The example Alistair used 
for MW Word - coded as a Procedural, with Classes listed, creates a 
series of MS Word objects which are invoked from that Procedural, which 
trundles through the procedural code without any paragraphs.

#2 - Richard's comment.

First I'd want to know what the topic was before I would commit. I'm 
sure you don't just intend to wrap the Procedural within OO and call it 
quits. You have some objective in mind - like the extending enhancement 
you suggest - which perhaps can be the only reason for OO-ing it ?

But it has to be carefully thought out. One area might be COBOL files or 
SQL - but I'll just stick to the first. (If we were thinking mainframe 
files, then we have a problem - all that JCL control as to  which disk 
sets to load operationally. Yes I saw sets of JCL cards back in the 
early to mid-70s, but other than that, my knowledge of JCL is a big fat 
zero). So keeping to the two we know about, Fujitsu and Micro Focus - 
yes or no - does the original code and the OO-wrapper have to be a pair, 
apples to apples, i.e. Fujitsu Procedural wrapped in a FJ-OO, or is it 
Micro Focus Procedural wrapped in MF-OO, or are you suggesting both 
Procedurals can be wrapped in a .Net OO ?

I can be imaginative but I'm also a cautious bugger when it comes to 
switching stuff. COBOL-wise, probably have a crack at one ISAM - but 
that does mean, subject to how the original was coded, (and particularly 
if it is written '74 style with no knowledge of three tier systems), and 
with references to that one file all over the place, then it should 
definitely be done cautiously.

(Don't believe me - take a look at my RM/COBOL code back in '80s. I 
designed it well, (Structured) but didn't know/appreciate Three-Tier at 
the time. So there are RM screen statements popping up all over the 
place. A nightmare. I can only conclude that the proper thing to do was 
a rewrite. So in that situation direct into OO would make more sense, or 
even wrap say the M/F Screen Section within OO, rather than go the whole 
hog to GUIs).

About 10 years back, I met an accountant here from S. Africa, and of all 
people, a bean-counter, favoured the BIG BANG approach ! Bloody idiot !

Jimmy
```

```
000010 IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.

000045               Eldersburg MD.
000050*REMARKS.

           ORGANIZATION IS INDEXED ACCESS IS
           DYNAMIC RECORD KEY IS KEYREC.

       FD  INFILE.
       01  MAIN-REC.
               05 KEYREC PIC 99.

000250 001-MAIN-PROCEDURE.
      *    OPEN I-O INFILE.
           COMPUTE RANDUM = FUNCTION RANDOM(8).
           COMPUTE KEYREC = RANDUM * 100.
           DISPLAY KEYREC.

      *    CLOSE INFILE.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: FUNCTION RANDOM.

- **From:** James Gavan <jgavan@shaw.ca>
- **Date:** 2010-11-10T16:52:08-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<KeGCo.20826$NM2.2619@newsfe22.iad>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<4f195c9e-8571-4297-837e-886523965a01@r14g2000yqa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<8ebd5cc6-869e-4d81-b376-6737853d79c3@l17g2000yqe.googlegroups.com> <S8FCo.13859$z41.9323@newsfe05.iad> <4f195c9e-8571-4297-837e-886523965a01@r14g2000yqa.googlegroups.com>`

```
On 11/10/2010 3:41 PM, john@wexfordpress.com wrote:
> On Nov 10, 5:37 pm, James Gavan<jga...@shaw.ca>  wrote:
>> On 11/10/2010 3:18 PM, j...@wexfordpress.com wrote:
…[67 more quoted lines elided]…
> See?

Yep ! That was a real quick response :-) But what actually is in that 
file. I've never used Randomizing.

Can't post the whole damn thing here, it's much too large. Written by 
Jerome Garfunkel using M/F Net Express. He, many moons ago, used to be 
on J4 and he's the brother of the singer. (His total example is 
screaming for a GUI Dialog).

I've extracted what he did for Random. The source is followed by the DOS 
screen results. If you are interested in getting his source for ALL 
functions then e-mail me and I'll send a zipfile.

Jimmy

*****************************************************************
* The Following program "Random" is nested in "Cobol89         *
*****************************************************************
*****************************************************************
* This program uses the following intrinsic functions.          *
*    RANDOM      CURRENT-DATE     NUMVAL        SQRT            *
*                                                               *
* The RANDOM functions has two formats - one with and argument  *
* and one without an argument.  When using the RANDOM function  *
* with an argument ("seed value") the same seed value will      *
* cause the RANDOM function to return the same random value.    *
* This is particularly useful for "regression testing" during   *
* program development.                                          *
*****************************************************************
  IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
  PROGRAM-ID. Random-JG.      *> That's Jerome not me :-) !
*AUTHOR.  Jerome Garfunkel.
  ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
  DATA DIVISION.
  WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
  1   random-return-values.
      3  first-in-random-sequence PIC 9(6)V9(12).
      3  next-in-random-sequence  PIC 9(6)V9(12).

  1   seed-value                  PIC 9(6)    VALUE 32767.

  1   square-root-of-seed         PIC  Z(6).9(6).

  1   repeat-response             PIC XXX.
      88  the-user-wants-another-demo  VALUE "Y" "y" "YES" "yes".

  1   current-date-and-time       PIC  x(21).

  PROCEDURE DIVISION.
*****************************************************************
* All program functions are controled from this procedure       *
*****************************************************************
  Program-Functions.

      PERFORM Random-Function-With-Seed
      PERFORM Random-Function-Without-Seed
      PERFORM Random-Function-With-Time-Seed
      PERFORM Repeat-Demo-Question

      IF the-user-wants-another-demo GO TO Program-Functions.

      EXIT PROGRAM.
      STOP RUN.
*****************************************************************
* The next procedure returns a Random value based on the seed-  *
* value (argument).  The same seed value causes the RANDOM      *
* function to return the same "random" value. This is           *
* particularly useful while regression testing                  *
* a program during development.                                 *
*****************************************************************
  Random-Function-With-Seed.

      INITIALIZE random-return-values.

      COMPUTE first-in-random-sequence
            = FUNCTION RANDOM (seed-value)
      END-COMPUTE.

      DISPLAY "The random value returned is "
              first-in-random-sequence.

*****************************************************************
* The next procedure returns a Random value with no seed-value  *
* (argument).  The next "random" number in sequence is returned *
* by the RANDOM function.                                       *
*****************************************************************
  Random-Function-Without-Seed.

      COMPUTE next-in-random-sequence
            = FUNCTION RANDOM
      END-COMPUTE.

      DISPLAY "The random value returned is "
               next-in-random-sequence.

*****************************************************************
* The next procedure is a more realistic version of the Random  *
* function that  might be used in applications.                 *
* The seed value that is used here is the "hundreth-of-seconds" *
* postions of the Current-Date function (positions 15, 16).     *
* Note the use of Reference Modification to reference the 15th  *
* and 16th positions from the 21 total positions of date/time   *
* information returned by the Current Date Function.  Also note *
* the Random function, when used with a "seed" value must       *
* provide an "integer" value for the argument.  The NUMVAL      *
* Function is used to convert the two positions of Current-date *
* into an integer for use in the Random Function .  Furthermore *
* the CURRENT-DATE function is "nested" in the NUMVAL function -*
* that is, the returned value of the CURRENT-DATE function      *
* serves as the argument for the NUMVAL function.               *
*****************************************************************
  Random-Function-With-Time-Seed.

      INITIALIZE random-return-values.

      COMPUTE seed-value
           =  FUNCTION NUMVAL (FUNCTION CURRENT-DATE (15 : 2))
           *  FUNCTION NUMVAL (FUNCTION CURRENT-DATE (15 : 2))

      COMPUTE square-root-of-seed
         =    FUNCTION SQRT (seed-value)

      COMPUTE first-in-random-sequence
           =  FUNCTION RANDOM (seed-value)

      END-COMPUTE.

      DISPLAY "The seed value used is "
              seed-value

      DISPLAY "The random value returned is "
              first-in-random-sequence.

*****************************************************************
* The next procedure determines if demo is to be run again.     *
* "y" or "Y" or "yes" or "YES" will re-run demo.  Anything else *
* will end the demo program.                                    *
*****************************************************************
  Repeat-Demo-Question.

      Display "Do you want to repeat demo for: "
              "function-to-demo - yes/no? "
              WITH NO ADVANCING

      ACCEPT  repeat-response.
  END PROGRAM Random-JG.

*****************************************
These are the results I got from runs :-
*****************************************
The random value returned is 000000288687194742
The random value returned is 000000085899342787
The seed value used is 000001
The random value returned is 000000476382794811
Do you want to repeat demo for: function-to-demo - yes/no? y
The random value returned is 000000476382794811
The random value returned is 000000547849351424
The seed value used is 003600
The random value returned is 000000874462619487
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: FUNCTION RANDOM.

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

- **References:** `<8ebd5cc6-869e-4d81-b376-6737853d79c3@l17g2000yqe.googlegroups.com> <S8FCo.13859$z41.9323@newsfe05.iad> <4f195c9e-8571-4297-837e-886523965a01@r14g2000yqa.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Wed, 10 Nov 2010 14:41:12 -0800 (PST), "john@wexfordpress.com"
<john@wexfordpress.com> wrote:

>000250 001-MAIN-PROCEDURE.
>      *    OPEN I-O INFILE.
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>See?

For a given seed, RANDOM will pull up a given value.   Typically you
use the most random seed you can for the first iteration, then use
your result as the next input.

e.g.:
MOVE FUNCTION CURRENT-DATE TO SYSTEM-DATE.             
MOVE SYSTEM-TIME-CC     TO SEED-VALUE                  
PERFORM 20 TIMES                                       
    COMPUTE MY-NUM     = FUNCTION RANDOM (SEED-VALUE)  
    COMPUTE SEED-VALUE = MY-NUM * 100000               
    DISPLAY 'SEED-VALUE"' SEED-VALUE '"'               
           
END-PERFORM                                            
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: FUNCTION RANDOM.

- **From:** "Bill Klein" <wmklein@noreply.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2010-11-10T17:20:07-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<FMFCo.371145$pX3.45199@en-nntp-11.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<8ebd5cc6-869e-4d81-b376-6737853d79c3@l17g2000yqe.googlegroups.com> <S8FCo.13859$z41.9323@newsfe05.iad>`

```
The rules for COBOL *require* that if you give the same "seed" number, then 
you MUST get the same "series" of returned values for the RANDOM function. 
The compilers are working "as required".

In order to get DIFFERENT numberts, you need to use different seed numbers. 
This is often done by using the time of day (seconds - for example) as the 
seed value. The more digits you use as the seed value, the more likely it is 
to get "unique" returned values.

See (for example), the statement at:

 http://publibfp.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr/BOOKS/IGY3LR50/7.1.38

"For a given seed value, the sequence of pseudorandom numbers is always the 
same. "

If you check the "language reference" (or ANSI/ISO Standards) you will see 
the same text.

"James Gavan" <jgavan@shaw.ca> wrote in message 
news:S8FCo.13859$z41.9323@newsfe05.iad...
> On 11/10/2010 3:18 PM, john@wexfordpress.com wrote:
>> When I use FUNCTION RANDOM the same value appears every time the
…[23 more quoted lines elided]…
> Jimmy, Calgary AB
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: FUNCTION RANDOM.

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@att.net>
- **Date:** 2010-11-11T00:11:21-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1dadnWy35ZSXFEbRnZ2dnUVZ5uKdnZ2d@giganews.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<FMFCo.371145$pX3.45199@en-nntp-11.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<8ebd5cc6-869e-4d81-b376-6737853d79c3@l17g2000yqe.googlegroups.com> <S8FCo.13859$z41.9323@newsfe05.iad> <FMFCo.371145$pX3.45199@en-nntp-11.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
On 11/10/2010 5:20 PM, Bill Klein wrote:
> The rules for COBOL *require* that if you give the same "seed" number, then
> you MUST get the same "series" of returned values for the RANDOM function.
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
> (snip)

In order to get a series of pseudo random numbers, the first instance of 
FUNCTION RANDOM must have a seed argument, and every subsequent 
invocation must omit the seed argument:

COMPUTE MY-RANDOM-NUMBER = FUNCTION RANDOM(SEED-VALUE)   <== first time

COMPUTE MY-RANDOM-NUMBER = FUNCTION RANDOM  <== every other time

If you're building a simulation and you need to test with the same 
series of pseudo random numbers, then always start with the same seed 
argument.  If you need a less predictable series of pseudo random 
numbers, then use something like time of day in milliseconds as your 
seed argument.

Don't forget that the pseudo random number returned is always a value 
between zero and one.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: FUNCTION RANDOM.

- **From:** Anonymous <cripto@ecn.org>
- **Date:** 2010-11-11T16:09:34+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20101111150934.466411A7925@www.ecn.org>`
- **References:** `<FMFCo.371145$pX3.45199@en-nntp-11.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
> The rules for COBOL *require* that if you give the same "seed" number,
> then you MUST get the same "series" of returned values for the RANDOM
> function.
> The compilers are working "as required".

I would add, this is true of every standard pseudo-random number generator.
They all work on the principle. You must provide (or use a default) seed and
given the same seed they will always produce the same sequence. This is how
pseudo-random number generators work. COBOL isn't unique in this, although
if there is some standard that specifies it, it's really just documenting
(also good!) the restriction/behavior of the underlying PRNG, not
introducing anything new.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: FUNCTION RANDOM.

- **From:** abrsvc <dansabrservices@yahoo.com>
- **Date:** 2010-11-11T06:02:29-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<0fa7d58e-0ac7-4294-881a-90f38075f04f@s11g2000prs.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<8ebd5cc6-869e-4d81-b376-6737853d79c3@l17g2000yqe.googlegroups.com> <4048f3ed-e292-4c86-a8a6-a691b43ed4f7@z9g2000yqz.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Nov 11, 6:51 am, Alistair Maclean
<alistair.j.l.macl...@googlemail.com> wrote:
> On Nov 10, 10:18 pm, "j...@wexfordpress.com" <j...@wexfordpress.com>
> wrote:
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
> available to do that (but I can't remember where to get it).

Please note that ALL values returned by any "random number generator"
are pseudo random.  Since these numbers are "generated", by definition
they are not truely random.  Different algorithms will generate longer
strings of non-repeatable values which appear to be somewhat random.
The longer the "repeat" interval, the more random the numbers.  There
are whole studies on differing generators.  The formula used by most
"random" functions is rather simple and has a relatively short repeat
string (in other words, the same pattern of values will be repeated
relatievly quickly).  For most applications this is sufficient.

As others have stated, in order to be able to debug the functions of a
program, most start with a fixed seed.  This will insure the same
sequence of random numbers be generated each run.  Once the debug
phase has completed, using a time value is the most common way of
seeding or starting the random number sequence that won't typically be
a repeatable sequence.

Dan
```

```
Bill,

your code is fine.

The problem is that you aren't checking for exceptions.

The first Open causes an exception if the file doesn't exist. Try running 
the same code having created the file. I'm betting it works as expected.

At the risk of teaching Granma' to suck eggs, you could create the file 
easily in a step before running the program, with the following DOS command:

ECHO 123456789 > datafile

Then run it.

You should really add a FILE STATUS to the FD and check it.

HTH,

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: OpenCOBOL problem

- **From:** James Gavan <jgavan@shaw.ca>
- **Date:** 2010-11-11T14:26:15-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<_bZCo.15684$Mk2.7824@newsfe13.iad>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<8k2rckFpfU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
On 11/11/2010 11:36 AM, Bill Gunshannon wrote:
> Anybody here doing stuff with OpenCOBOL?  I have a problem that one
> would think would be easy to fix.  I can't seem to open a file for
> input.
>
> Here is my test program.

Ahhh Richard's reply was the giveaway :-

 From my class that has the M/F file-status error codes :-

05 pic x(L2) value "30I-O error/Data check parity err.".
05 pic x(L2) value "34Boundary violation              ".
05 pic x(L2) value "35Open IO/INPUT/EXTEND non-optionl".

Here's your program using M/F Net Express :-

--------------------------------------------------

Program-ID.    Tfile.
Author.        Bill Gunshannon.

File-Control.
     Select Datafile Assign To 'datafile'.

Data Division.

File Section.
FD  Datafile
     Data Record Is In-Record.

01  In-Record  Pic X(9).

Procedure Division.

Open Output DataFile       *> Add these two lines
Close DataFile             *>  ..   ..  ..  ..
Display "Open File".
Open Input Datafile.
Display "Close File".
Close Datafile
Display "Exit Program".
Stop Run.

I didn't invoke my File Status class, just Procedural to see what would 
happen. First time around, tried it without my two additional lines. 
Surprisingly, never seen it before, but M/F came back with their own 
Message - Error 13 File doesn't exist

Don't know whether Open Source has used some of the PC-based CBL_ 
routines available in Fujitsu or Micro Focus, but I use :-

Call CBL_CHECK_FILE_EXISTS using filename returning Result

if Result is incorrect then you need an Open-New-File routine, those 
first two lines.

Did you test TinyCOBOL against an EXISTING file - ????

Got caught years ago. Wrote part of an application where I used M/F 
Directives to compress records. Worked fine. Looked at it some eight 
months later testing it and it went belly-up.

Famous "Well it used to work". Contacted M/F Forum they were helpful but 
no joy. Some further six months went by - and then it clicked.
On the re-vamp, I had excluded the compress Directive. Without the 
directive the new version couldn't expand records to their true length !

Jimmy
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: OpenCOBOL problem

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-11-11T18:00:43-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<227e30b3-ee8c-4a99-b931-fc867826c528@g4g2000prj.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<8k2rckFpfU1@mid.individual.net> <_bZCo.15684$Mk2.7824@newsfe13.iad> <8k3cu7FpfU8@mid.individual.net>`

```
On Nov 12, 12:35 pm, billg...@cs.uofs.edu (Bill Gunshannon) wrote:
> In article <_bZCo.15684$Mk2.7...@newsfe13.iad>,


> Actually, everything I  found says 35 is a "boundry violation", whatever
> that is.

What 'everything' is that ?  34 is boundary violation. With ANS85 you
will get '35' for file not found, or '05' if it is not found and is
optional.

My run of your program give a 35 error.

Note that OpenCOBOL can work.

30 implies 'failed' and 'no extra information' which implies that the
file handler is not installed, or not found.

OpenCOBOL can use various file handlers including BerkelyDB or VBisam
(I think).

--with-db1        use Berkeley DB 1.85 (libdb-1.85)
--with-db         use Berkeley DB 3.0 or later (default)
--with-lfs64      use large file system for file I/O (default)

If it can't find the libraries then it may fail in ways that match
your results.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: OpenCOBOL problem

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** billg999@cs.uofs.edu (Bill Gunshannon)

```
staff at the University or are you an instructor. If you are a teacher, 
Christ help your students if you can lose your cool over something this 
trivial and condemn a compiler as being defective.

Now make the bloody effort to read the Open Source COBOL manual, which I 
did for the first time. References to your problem :-

4.7 		File Status Table
6.32 		OPEN
7.3.1.14 	CBL_CHECK_FILE_EXISTS
8.1. 		FileStat-Msgs.cpy  - 35 FILE NOT FOUND

The only thing wrong with my quote from my File-Status Table

05 pic x(L2) value "35Open IO/INPUT/EXTEND non-optionl".,

was that I paraphrased it. The full M/F text for a 35 IS :-

35 An OPEN operation with the I-O, INPUT, or EXTEND phrases has been 
tried on a non-OPTIONAL file that is not present. (Take it as read - 
that is the ANSI definition).

If you aren't using File-Status checks with DECLARATIVES, (which I 
personally consider the pits), or preferably a routine that lets you 
call their File-Status message table, may I suggest that you should. If 
you are an Instructor, you aren't giving your students good advice. 
Prepare them for this problem, regardless of compiler showing literals 
for file errors. You will save them a lot of unnecessary aggravation in 
the early part of their careers.

You came here for FREE advice - and dished out your aggravation.

Jimmy
```

#### ↳ Re: OpenCOBOL problem

- **From:** "HeyBub" <heybub@NOSPAMgmail.com>
- **Date:** 2010-11-11T16:06:23-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<x4SdnRo0V4589UHRnZ2dnUVZ_t-dnZ2d@earthlink.com>`
- **References:** `<8k2rckFpfU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Bill Gunshannon wrote:
> Anybody here doing stuff with OpenCOBOL?  I have a problem that one
> would think would be easy to fix.  I can't seem to open a file for
…[69 more quoted lines elided]…
>

The contents of the File-Control paragraph are implementor-defined and vary 
across compilers. The default organization may be way different between 
compilers (SEQUENTIAL or something else). The "assign to" clause may 
reference a data-name defined in working storage, an external parameter, or 
be the actual name of the file itself.

And so on.

So, then, your "dataname" may be trying to reference a file that does not 
exist, cannot be found, is not defined, or whose attributes do not match the 
(implied) definition.

I suggest you review the definitions of the File-Control paragraph for the 
compiler(s) you are using. You will find marked differences in their syntax 
and implementation.

Or it could be something else altogether, possibly involving a jar of 
mayonnaise.
```

```
I wouldn't wish to pour oil on troubled waters but:

1. You show 'Open File' appears twice in the program output although
that display is only executed once in your program. I presume that is
the famous red herring (Clupea harengus rudis to biologists).

2. File status code 30 is an open error with no further information
available.
I don't know how clever TinyCobol and OpenCobol are but it may be for
any one of a host of reasons from file does not exist; to the file
being empty at time of opening; to the record contents being different
from the record description definition (if you have a record of three
characters long or a record that is variable in length) to ....   It
might help to show us the contents of the file.
```

#### ↳ Re: OpenCOBOL problem

- **From:** Brian Tiffin <btiffin@canada.com>
- **Date:** 2010-11-20T22:39:28-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6e23b0ce-2aee-401f-9a0f-eb9ad3ba650e@z19g2000yqb.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<8k2rckFpfU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
On Nov 11, 1:36 pm, billg...@cs.uofs.edu (Bill Gunshannon) wrote:
> Anybody here doing stuff with OpenCOBOL?  I have a problem that one
> would think would be easy to fix.  I can't seem to open a file for
…[70 more quoted lines elided]…
> Scranton, Pennsylvania   |         #include <std.disclaimer.h>  

Just in case; see http://opencobol.add1tocobol.com/#assign as you may
have an environment variable in between you and your local file.
OpenCOBOL follows a configuration setting.

# If yes, file names are resolved at run time using
#   environment variables.
# For example, given ASSIGN TO "DATAFILE", the actual
#   file name will be
#  1. the value of environment variable 'DD_DATAFILE' or
#  2. the value of environment variable 'dd_DATAFILE' or
#  3. the value of environment variable 'DATAFILE' or
#  4. the literal "DATAFILE"
# If no, the value of the assign clause is the file name.
#
# Value: 'yes', 'no'
filename-mapping: yes

Umm, just in case.

Cheers,
Brian
```

## Thread: File extensions in Windows — 27 this month / 28 total

### File extensions in Windows

- **From:** James Gavan <jgavan@shaw.ca>
- **Date:** 2010-11-15T13:50:01-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<12hEo.16369$ME5.476@newsfe15.iad>`

```

Does anybody know of a neat way of finding file extensions when using 
Explorer. Column 1, Explorer lists the filename but not the file 
extension, followed by Size and a file type description. Background :-

I've known for quite a number of years that M/F Net Express has the 
ability to generate templates of OO classes and methods. Having created 
a class template, from the IDE you can click on OO Method and it adds a 
blank template method to your class. Like anybody else I have my own 
preference for layout, and getting at those templates I'm reasonably 
confident I can achieve what I want by changing the text of the M/F 
Templates - BUT FIRSTLY saving the M/F set of templates to a backup 
folder, in case anything goes wrong. In addition to what I've indicated 
here there is one template which generates some 7 different versions of 
'True' OLE classes (Client or Server, generate Registry entries etc....)

I tried to find them knowing they are written using MS Word - couldn't; 
obviously they must be in an M/F directory which in my case starts at :-

\Program Files\Merant\Net Express\Base.

obvious search key seemed to be - *.doc, starting at Merant if you like. 
Only one comes back - a reference to an OLE Demo in their samples 
programs. I eventually tracked them down :-

\Merant\Net Express\Base\Bin - 14 of them

I tried using the Help within MS Word to see if it spelled out 
extensions, some 12 suggestions but not one relating exactly to what the 
extension is for MS Word Wizards - this latter type only became apparent 
when I found the 14 above.

I haven't found anything in Windows that directly lets me get at 
extensions. Fortunately I have one of those old programs from PC 
Magazine where you laboriously keyed in the hex values and a checksum 
tells you if you had made an error. For DOS it's called DR.com 
(Directory Listing) - put it into the above directory and it displayed 
those MS Word Wizards as 'abcdefg.wiz'. Any way in Windows to get that ?

Now I know where they are I can dabble to making changes to the M/F source.

Jimmy, Calgary AB
```

#### ↳ Re: File extensions in Windows

- **From:** "Charles Hottel" <chottel@earthlink.net>
- **Date:** 2010-11-15T16:17:25-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<37idnXK3dYPHPnzRnZ2dnUVZ_oednZ2d@earthlink.com>`
- **References:** `<12hEo.16369$ME5.476@newsfe15.iad>`

```

"James Gavan" <jgavan@shaw.ca> wrote in message 
news:12hEo.16369$ME5.476@newsfe15.iad...
>
> Does anybody know of a neat way of finding file extensions when using 
…[40 more quoted lines elided]…
> Jimmy, Calgary AB

On my Windows Xp system:

Windows Explore > Tools > Folder Options

    View tab: uncheck hide extensions for known file types
    View Tab: show hidden files and folders (may also be of use)

    File types tab:  shows association sof file types with programs
```

```
then shown, one can change the Read Only and other attributes.
```

```
On 11/16/2010 4:09 PM, James Gavan wrote:
> (snip)
> Boy ! Has this one gone off on a tangent, Charlie :-)
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> Hidden, Read-Only etc. ?

At the command prompt, type "ATTRIB /?" to get help.

Displays or changes file attributes.

ATTRIB [+R | -R] [+A | -A ] [+S | -S] [+H | -H] [drive:][path][filename]
        [/S [/D]]

   +   Sets an attribute.
   -   Clears an attribute.
   R   Read-only file attribute.
   A   Archive file attribute.
   S   System file attribute.
   H   Hidden file attribute.
   [drive:][path][filename]
       Specifies a file or files for attrib to process.
   /S  Processes matching files in the current folder
       and all subfolders.
   /D  Processes folders as well.

I would probably open a CMD.EXE window, navigate to the "my pictures" 
folder and type something like this:

ATTRIB -R *.*

That would select all files ("*.*") in the current directory, and turn 
the READ-ONLY attribute OFF.

But if you can see the file in Windows Explorer, right-click on it and 
then click on "properties", then if necessary select the "General" tab. 
You should be able to clear the read-only and hidden attributes by 
unchecking them.  You can select the advanced tab to uncheck the Archive 
attribute.

You might try setting the READ-ONLY attribute ON, and then OFF, by 
checking it Read-only box, clicking on the Apply button, then unchecking 
the Read-only box and clicking on the Apply button again.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: File extensions in Windows

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-11-18T00:29:01+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8khsjvF2p9U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<12hEo.16369$ME5.476@newsfe15.iad> <37idnXK3dYPHPnzRnZ2dnUVZ_oednZ2d@earthlink.com> <g935e6lqdt4c2hef1fo5hne6s135e7ikls@4ax.com>`

```
Howard Brazee wrote:
> On Mon, 15 Nov 2010 16:17:25 -0500, "Charles Hottel"
> <chottel@earthlink.net> wrote:
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…
> drive.

What NOT to do:

1. Don't try changing folder Read-Only attributes. You can't do it (unless 
it is a custom folder) and it doesn't mean anything anyway on an XP system.

2. Don't try downloading IRFanView. While this is an excellent package, it 
won't solve your problem. A package you COULD consider using is Picasa. 
Particularly good for dealing with files to be transferred between MAC and 
PC via USB stick. (I know you have a MAC, Howard.) Picasa is a free package: 
http://www.soft82.com/download/Windows/Picasa

As you know, I wouldn't recommend it unless it was good.

What you SHOULD DO:

1. Remove the +R attribute from the image file, if it is set. (Oops, sorry, 
I just noted above you already checked that...)

2. Make sure the account you are using to access the photos has the 
necessary permissions. Open MyComputer, then right click on the C: drive (or 
whichever drive you have your photos on) and open the "Properties" tab. Open 
the "Security" tab and see if the account you are using when you access the 
pictures has full permissions. If it hasn't, give it full permissions. Make 
sure the Administrator group has full permissions.


More information needed:

1. Is it only .JPGS?
2. Are .GIFs affected also?

If GIFS are OK, try the following:

    1. Open one of the affected .JPGs in Windows Fax and Picture viewer. (Or 
double-click on the .JPG file in Windows Explorer. Assuming you have .JPGs 
associated with this standard Windows program (it's the default.))
     2. Having opened the "unrotatable" image, hold Ctrl down and click on 
the red x in the top right corner.

Now re-open it and see if it can be rotated.

.JPG files created on a digital camera contain something called EXIF 
metadata tags which tells software looking at the image which way it should 
be orientated, as well as a bunch of other information which would surprise 
most photgraphers using digital cameras.... (The Picasa package noted above 
recognises EXIF metadata, but you may find that a lossless .JPG rotator will 
do the trick. I haven't used this one but, apparently, it is good... 
http://annystudio.com/software/jpeglosslessrotator/

If GIFs won't rotate either:

1. Check the space available. Rotating a 4MB image can take a lot of disk 
and memory.

If none of the above suggestions solve your problem please mail me 
privately.

Pete.
```

### Microfocus Warning/Errors Line Numbers

- **From:** Derek Schrock <dereks@lifeofadishwasher.com>
- **Date:** 2010-11-17T11:43:48-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

```
Does anyone know if there's a compiler directive for MC SE 4.0 SP2
that reports the original line number before copy books are included
when an error or warning is reported?
```

#### ↳ Re: Microfocus Warning/Errors Line Numbers

- **From:** James Gavan <jgavan@shaw.ca>
- **Date:** 2010-11-17T18:01:11-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<tV_Eo.32251$lL3.21536@newsfe08.iad>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<738b690c-78f2-4082-bc35-621da8d7da1e@n30g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<738b690c-78f2-4082-bc35-621da8d7da1e@n30g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`

```
On 11/17/2010 12:43 PM, Derek Schrock wrote:
> Does anyone know if there's a compiler directive for MC SE 4.0 SP2
> that reports the original line number before copy books are included
> when an error or warning is reported?

I'd been inclined to say 'No'. I take it 'SE" above refers to Server 
Express ? It's copacetic with Net Express, so they will both do the same 
thing.

Not quite what you are after, but it illustrates - I have originals of 
some of my classes in a separate folder \Copylib - these are a bunch 
which are constantly re-used with different projects, in Develpment ode 
- I've no intent of producing DLLs or EXEs. For compatibility, if 
changing \Copylib\Program-A I compile in that folder\project and ANY 
errors including errors in the structure of any copyfiles get reported 
with sequential line numbering for the WHOLE source of Program-A.

Now I might have a small Project, like 99-Bottles coming up which uses 
\Copylib\Program-A and the Bottles project has a file :-

*>----------- Program-A.COB-------------
copy "\Copylib\Program-A.cbl".
*>--------------------------------------

That one-liner is added to the Bottles project and is shown in the IDE 
for Bottles and using the Alt + F2 brings up the source of Program-A, 
(the original). Note, only yesterday hit on the idea of giving the file 
above the extension ...COB to differentiate between the receiving 
project with ....CBL files and those ....COB files which refer to \Copylib.

OK, so sometimes I'll make changes to what is if you like currently 
Program-A.COB because I'm cross referencing to other programs ...COB or 
more likely the traditional ....CBL in the Bottles Project.

I'll get errors perhaps, but like you wont get correct references to the 
prime text or copyfiles because they don't match. I have to get back to 
\Copylib\Program-A.cbl and do a re-compile and that takes me direct to 
the error lines.

I said 'No' at the beginning, because when first designing DIRECTIVES, I 
very much doubt M/F took into account dumb users like me buggering 
around with project structures :-).

You could raise the question in the old M/F Forum, but they appear to 
have tailed-off on that, particularly Net Express. Might well be 
different for Server Express.

Jimmy, Calgary AB
```

```
ERRFORMAT(2) may have the desired effect. I've only tried it on Windows :

 >cobol myapp nognt list() errformat(2);
Micro Focus Net Express
Version 6.0.11055  Copyright (C) 1984-2010 Micro Focus (IP) Limited.
URN AXCGG/AA0/00000
     50     accept svr
**    COBCH0012S Operand SVR is not declared  : myapp.cbl(27,21)
     58     END-EXEC
**    COBES0109S SVR is not a data item.   : myapp.cbl(35,19)
* Checking complete - errors found

The "50" indicates the listing line number including the expanded 
copybook, but the myapp.cbl(27,21) shows the real source line and column.

The documentation can be found at 
http://documentation.microfocus.com:8080/help/index.jsp?topic=/com.microfocus.eclipse.infocenter.studee60ux.sp01/HRCDRHCDIRCI.html 


Hope that helps,
SimonT.
```

<a id="t-8072b4ed3b"></a>
## Thread: COBOL and high energy physics — 4 msgs

### COBOL and high energy physics

- **From:** Brian Tiffin <btiffin@canada.com>
- **Date:** 2010-11-20T22:49:53-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<83d7194a-4999-4acb-a009-608adf75d7ee@s4g2000yql.googlegroups.com>`

```
If you ever feel like taking a break from business and relaxing in a
nice petrabyte sized pile of subatomic analysis data, meet ROOT/CINT.
http://root.cern.ch/drupal/content/cint  Another gift to the world
from CERN.

It turns out that OpenCOBOL subprograms can be loaded into and
interactively tested using the very capable CINT C/C++ interpreter.
CINT was written to allow scientists to write scripts and interact at
a console with huge data sets.  And now that power can be leveraged to
test out subprograms.

On a Fedora 14 system, yum install root.

Then given

OCOBOL*>>SOURCE FORMAT IS FIXED
      *>
***************************************************************
      *> Author:    Brian Tiffin
      *> Date:      20101119
      *> Purpose:   Pass arguments to ROOT/CINT invoked subprograms
      *> Tectonics: cobc -fimplicit-init -C cobparams.cob
      *>
***************************************************************
       identification division.
       program-id. cobparams.

       data division.
       linkage section.
       01 a-number usage binary-long.

      *>
***************************************************************
       procedure division using by reference a-number.
       display a-number end-display
       move a-number to return-code
       goback.
       end program cobparams.

and then the commands

$ cobc -fimplicit-init -C cobparams.cob
$ root -l
root [0] gSystem->Load("/usr/local/lib/libcob.so");
root [1] .L cobparams.c+
root [2] int a = 0;
root [3] int d = 42;
root [4] a = cobparams((unsigned char*)&d);
+0000000042
root [5] printf("%d\n", a);
42
root [6]

You get interactive access to COBOL subprograms, and if the desire
takes, access to a tremendous framework for exploring the quantum
universe while pondering while payroll was off by 12 cents.

Cheers,
Brian
```

```
On Nov 22, 11:22 pm, Paul <paul-nospamatall.rauler...@mac.com> wrote:
> On 2010-11-21 00:49:53 -0600, Brian Tiffin said:
> That's just cool Brian! Thanks. -Paul
…[61 more quoted lines elided]…
> > Brian

I had a chance to revisit.

OCOBOL*>>SOURCE FORMAT IS FIXED
      *> *********************************************************
      *> Author:    Brian Tiffin
      *> Date:      20101119
      *> Purpose:   Pass arguments to ROOT/CINT invoked subprograms
      *> Tectonics: cobc -fimplicit-init -C cobparams.cob
      *> *********************************************************
       identification division.
       program-id. cobparams.

       data division.
       linkage section.
       01 a-number usage binary-long.

      *> *********************************************************
       procedure division using by reference a-number.
       display a-number end-display
       move a-number to return-code
       goback.
       end program cobparams.

      *> *********************************************************
      *> *********************************************************

       REPLACE ==ARRAYSIZE== BY ==450==.

       identification division.
       program-id. cobfloats.

       data division.
       working-storage section.
       01 cnt pic 999.
       01 val usage float-long.
       01 xes.
          02 an-x usage float-long occurs ARRAYSIZE times.
       01 yes.
          02 an-y usage float-long occurs ARRAYSIZE times.

       linkage section.
       01 vxes.
          02 an-x usage float-long occurs ARRAYSIZE times.
       01 vyes.
          02 an-y usage float-long occurs ARRAYSIZE times.

      *> *********************************************************
       procedure division using by reference vxes, vyes.
       perform varying cnt from 1 by 1 until cnt >= ARRAYSIZE
           compute val = cnt * function random() end-compute
           move cnt to an-x in xes(cnt)
           move val to an-y in yes(cnt)
       end-perform
       move xes to vxes.
       move yes to vyes.
       move cnt to return-code
       goback.
       end program cobfloats.

and then

$ cobc -fimplicit-init -C cobparams.cob
$ vi cobparams.c
... add a single line
...   #pragma K&R
... to lighten up CINT's type safety for ease of use at the console
$ root -l
root [0] gSystem->Load("/usr/local/lib/libcob.so");
root [1] .L cobparams.c+
root [2] int a = 0; double x[450]; double y[450];
root [3] a = cobfloats(&x, &y);
root [4] a
(int)450
root [5] printf("%f %f\n", x[42], y[42]);
43.000000 8.232543
root [6] TGraph *graph1 = new TGraph(450, x, y);
root [7] graph1->Draw("A*");
root [8] TGraphPolar *polar1 = new TGraphPolar(450, x, y);
root [9] polar1->SetLineColor(2);
root [10] polar1->Draw("AOL");

The Draw() ROOT methods display some nice plots.  Interactive ROOT
graphs.  See
http://opencobol.add1tocobol.com/#graphing-sample for some
screenshots

Thanks very much to the great people at CERN.  Writing that part of
the FAQ was fun.  And I'll opine my belief that it opens the doors to
some very sophisticated interactive analysis tools for COBOL working
storage.  And yep; just cool.

Cheers,
Brian
```

## Thread: PERFORM without UNTIL — 13 this month / 15 total

_Topics: [`Language features and syntax`](topics.md#syntax)_

### PERFORM without UNTIL

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>
- **Date:** 2010-11-24T16:16:16-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4CED3A50.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com>`

```
Interesting.  I was looking through one of the IBM Language Environment
sample COBOL programs and came upon one with the following code:

  PERFORM                                                
    CALL "CEEGQDT" USING CURRENT-CONDITION               
                       Q-DATA-TOKEN FC                   
    IF SEVERITY > 0 THEN                                 
       DISPLAY "CALL to CEEGQDT failed with "            
               "Severity = " SEVERITY                    
       DISPLAY "                and message "            
               "number   = " MSGNO                       
       GOBACK                                            
    END-IF                                               
    SET ADDRESS OF Q-DATA-PTRS TO Q-DATA-TOKEN           
    SET ADDRESS OF ABEND-CODE TO Q-DATA-ABEND-CODE-PTR   
    EVALUATE ABEND-CODE                                 
       WHEN 777                                         
         DISPLAY "Severe Error!  Condition Handling "   
                 "should not get control for IMS Abends"
         SET PERCOLATE TO TRUE                          
       WHEN OTHER                                       
         CONTINUE                                       
    END-EVALUATE                                        
  END-PERFORM                                           

What's weird?  There's a PERFORM, but no UNTIL!
And it even compiles.  I wonder what their reason behind doing this was.  I
could be mistaken, but I don't imagine the program would behave any
differently with the PERFORM and END-PERFORM removed.
```

#### ↳ Re: PERFORM without UNTIL

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2010-11-25T03:36:38+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<icklk6$hjg$1@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<4CED3A50.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com>`

```
In article <4CED3A50.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com>,
Frank Swarbrick <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote:
>Interesting.  I was looking through one of the IBM Language Environment
>sample COBOL programs and came upon one with the following code:
>
>  PERFORM                                                

[snip]

>  END-PERFORM                                           
>
>What's weird?  There's a PERFORM, but no UNTIL!

Eh?  What's that, sonny?  What's weird is that there's a PERFORM and no 
nearby paragraph-name... no, wait, sorry, that's been fair play for a 
quarter-century now.

>And it even compiles.  I wonder what their reason behind doing this was.

I barely know my own reasons for doing anything, let alone anyone 
else's... but it struck me, stylistically, as a chunk of code that should 
be executed by an EVALUATE or a complex IF.

DD
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: PERFORM without UNTIL

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2010-11-25T03:54:36-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<cnqHo.479969$Is6.35101@en-nntp-13.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<4CED3A50.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com> <icklk6$hjg$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```
There are two reasons (thatI can think of) why such code might exist:

1) Simply to indicate a "logical block" of  code.
2) Because it used to be an "out-of-line PERFORM that someone moved in-line

Of course, there if you have an out-of-line PERFORM (with no UNTIL) it does 
the same thing as moving all the code "inline", too (assuming you use corret 
scope-terminators and remove all periods).

Without seeing the specific code example and knowing some of the LE 
documenation, it wouldn't surprise me if this code was done to "match" some 
C code or other language "logical block" structure.

<docdwarf@panix.com> wrote in message news:icklk6$hjg$1@reader1.panix.com...

…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: PERFORM without UNTIL

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>
- **Date:** 2010-11-26T15:16:19-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4CEFCF43.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com>`
- **References:** `<4CED3A50.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com> <icklk6$hjg$1@reader1.panix.com> <4CEF79DE.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com> <bae86a37-b284-4e73-8653-e3ed66f66bcf@k14g2000pre.googlegroups.com> <icp76c$gj7$1@news.eternal-september.org>`

```
Could have been an interesting alternative to END- statements in COBOL 1985.
 For example...

IF SOME-CONDITION
    PERFORM
        PERFORM SOMETHING
        PERFORM SOMETHING-ELSE
    END-PERFORM
ELSE
    PERFORM
        PERFORM SOMETHING-ELSE
        PERFORM SOMETHING
    END-PERFORM

Of course it'd probably also have to have a rule that IF and ELSE can be
followed by only a single "statement" (with the PERFORM block being
considered a statement), pretty much like C et al.  But not like prior
versions of COBOL, so I can see why they didn't go that way!

Frank
```

```
>On Thu, 25 Nov 2010 03:36:38 +0000 (UTC), docdwarf@panix.com () wrote:
>
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>I enjoyed that response.

It was a variant based on a theme over a decade old... from 
<http://groups.google.com/group/comp.lang.rexx/msg/29d1b77320d7bfc7> and 
an exchange between Mr Hamasaki - may he sleep with the angels! - and me:

--begin quoted text (dated 19 Mar 1999)

>Other may prefer programming languages with more modern
>constructs.

Others may, sure... but let them *try* to get some code past a review and 
implemented into Prod!

'What is *this* stuff?  EVALUATE TRUE WHEN cond-1 imperative statement... 
you call this COBOL?!?'

'Oh, please, Mr Standards-and-Practises Reviewmeister, it is exactly what 
is allowed by the ANSI '85 Standard.'

'ANSI '85?  Crap, I *knew* things were goin' ta hell in a handbasket when 
we allowed them fancy ANSI '74 constructs in a couple a' years back... 
look, 1985 is only 14 years ago, we oughta wait until the technology is 
Really Proven before we implement it.  Go back and rewrite this in *real* 
COBOL, then try again.'

--end quoted text

DD
```

## Thread: Is INCLUDE a keyword in COBOL? — 26 msgs

### Is INCLUDE a keyword in COBOL?

- **From:** Pavel <p.pleva@sh.cvut.cz>
- **Date:** 2010-11-26T12:16:46+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ico501$20m7$1@ns.felk.cvut.cz>`

```
Does anyone know whether 'INCLUDE' has some special meaning in any dialect or 
version of Cobol? In another words: is it 100% safe to use it for variable name?

The only usage I found is in preprocessor directives: 'EXEC SQL INCLUDE' and 
'++INCLUDE' (PANVALET).

Thanks

Pavel
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Is INCLUDE a keyword in COBOL?

- **From:** Alistair <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2010-11-26T06:57:16-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4248d4c5-5cbc-440c-bf2a-9c8f66d8759d@p7g2000prb.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<ico501$20m7$1@ns.felk.cvut.cz> <1836c0b1-1163-45ae-98d4-9e3ed283efe9@p11g2000vbn.googlegroups.com> <icobaq$22ro$2@ns.felk.cvut.cz>`

```
On Nov 26, 1:04 pm, Pavel <p.pl...@sh.cvut.cz> wrote:
> > A simple query on GOOGLE using the terms:
> >     cobol include
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
> Pavel

Au contraire.

The INCLUDE mentioned is to do with the SQL pre-processor. This runs
(Cobol 101) as part of the compilation process to take EXEC...END-EXEC
code constructs (used for CICS and DB2 on IBM Cobol) and convert them
in to Cobol which the compiler can understand. If you use INCLUDE in a
program which is pre-processed to convert DB2 SQL statements in an IBM
Cobol program to Cobol code which can be understood by the compile
step then you will get an error message about the pre-processor being
unable to find the include member and the compilation will stop at
that point.

If you are not using SQL and do not do any pre-processing and are not
using Panvalet (or Librarian) then a simple check of the Cobol manual
will reveal whether INCLUDE is a reserved word in the dialect of Cobol
that you are using. If it is not a reserved word and bearing in mind
all the crap above about pre-processing then it is safe to use it as a
data-item name. I wouldn't but them Im not brave.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Is INCLUDE a keyword in COBOL?

```
Alistair, thanks for your explanation, but I think there's been a little 
misunderstanding. I know what EXEC...END-EXEC and PANVALET statements are and 
how they are processed. My question was: is it safe to write (e.g.):
       01  INCLUDE PIC X(8) VALUE 'INCLUDE '.
(This statement has obviously no relation to DB2 SQL prepro and I believe it is 
irrelevant whether any EXEC SQL appears in the same source.)

it for Enterprise Cobol and I also googled queries like "cobol include". I
```

```
On 11/26/2010 11:05 AM, Pavel wrote:
> Alistair, thanks for your explanation, but I think there's been a little
> misunderstanding. I know what EXEC...END-EXEC and PANVALET statements
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Kind of nice when the person spells out what they are really after. In 
the COBOL Standards INCLUDE is not a Reserved word, it doesn't appear in 
any of the dialects used by Micro Focus in their on-line LRMs for Net 
Express V5.1 As a separate issue from Reserved Words, the only entry 
used with a Directive, is the word "++INCLUDE". But continue to use it, 
and these wont give you any heartburn :-

01 ws-INCLUDE PIC X(8) VALUE 'INCLUDE '.
01 IN-CLUDE PIC X(8) VALUE 'INCLUDE '.
01 INKLUDE PIC X(8) VALUE 'INCLUDE '.

Jimmy, Calgary AB
```

```
Alistair (et al),
  I think that I agree with the statment that using INCLUDE as a 
user-defined word (e.g.data-name or procedure name) is "unwise" and that 
using something like WS-INCLUDE or "NCLUDE" (no I) is good "preventive" 
coding.

However, to the best of my knowledge all compiler that include "built-in" 
SQL or CIDS processors distinguish between words INSICE an EXEC ... END-EXEC 
statement and those outside of it.  For example, UNION or JOIN can be used 
as COBOL user-defined words in such environments.

"Alistair Maclean" <alistair.j.l.maclean@googlemail.com> wrote in message 
news:ec4bce0a-fc17-4b20-bd87-2abec359d3f1@k38g2000vbc.googlegroups.com...
```

```
In article <icostp$28sl$1@ns.felk.cvut.cz>, Pavel  <p.pleva@sh.cvut.cz> wrote:
>Alistair, thanks for your explanation, but I think there's been a little 
>misunderstanding. I know what EXEC...END-EXEC and PANVALET statements are and 
>how they are processed. My question was: is it safe to write (e.g.):
>       01  INCLUDE PIC X(8) VALUE 'INCLUDE '.

My answer is, given what's been shown, 'no'.  If you need a literal like 
that it might be safest to call it WS-INCLUDE or WK-INCLUDE or 
LIT-INCLUDE.

(That it can be done is not always reason that it should be done, as many 
who've run across 'Look, Ma, I'm a Programmer!' code might say.)

DD
```

#### ↳ Re: Is INCLUDE a keyword in COBOL?

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-11-27T10:43:44+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8lao0iFn74U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<ico501$20m7$1@ns.felk.cvut.cz>`

```
Pavel wrote:
> Does anyone know whether 'INCLUDE' has some special meaning in any
> dialect or version of Cobol? In another words: is it 100% safe to use
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> Pavel

From time to time when writing COBOL this issue rears its head.

As there are some 650 reserved words in COBOL on average (varies with 
different dialects, of course) it would be tedious to try and memorise them 
all, especially when some of them are seldom used or not immediately 
obvious.

The wise old grey badger who taught me COBOL when I was just a bright-eyed 
whipper-snapper advised as follows:

"If you want to use a dataname and suspect it might be a reserved word, put 
a hyphen in it."

As that was in 1967 and COBOL has expanded a bit since then, his advice 
might not be sound today, but it can be modified so it would be. For example 
if you add a prefix or suffix to the name that includes a hyphen AND 
something not run-of-the-mill, you can be pretty certain that what you have 
will cause no problems.  (XX-INCLUDE)

I just checked the list of reserved words I use when parsing COBOL source 
and found INCLUDE is in it. However, that may not mean anything for the 
version you are using.

Pete.
```

```
If Fox said it, you can believe it. You can take it to the bank. You can

God talks to us via Fox.

As for the Computerworld article:

1. "Once within a network -- initially delivered via an infected USB 
device --" how could they know the mode of transmission was a USB? It could 
have been a CD or a floppy or some other device. Maybe even someone TYPED it 
in! They don't say. At least the Fox article admitted the vector was 
unknown.

certificates". Fox named the two certifying agencies - Computerworld did 
not.

engineers and technicians were arrested for sabotage or simply disappeared, 
and minders were assigned to the rest of the staff, plunging moral down the 
toilet.

This last observation was left out of the Computerworld article and, to my 
mind, is almost as interesting as the first part.

No, the Computerworld article, while it has more quotes from shocked 
experts, is but a poor shadow of the more excellent Fox report.
```

```
believed that Stuxnet -- whose roots were later traced as far back as

malware."""

acquire the worm and then bring it back to the plant."""

'Flash Drive' == 'USB flash drive'
```

## Thread: Change alphanumeric field to numeric field — 2 msgs

### Change alphanumeric field to numeric field

- **From:** GARY <gcotterl@co.riverside.ca.us>
- **Date:** 2010-11-28T09:07:42-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<cf4d6b89-2db7-4c33-a39d-265a93bf1e18@z26g2000prf.googlegroups.com>`

```
A COBOL program produced records with this format:

01 OUTPUT-AREA.
         03 ASMT-NBR-O   PIC S9(09)    VALUE +0  COMP-3.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: text file without CRLF

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-11-29T11:59:27-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<f42c970e-c385-4338-9f9f-97dd662d0133@o11g2000prf.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<4cf3c969$0$13734$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <id0jio$q4$00$1@news.t-online.com> <4cf3d9d5$0$13731$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <4d21937a-d10e-4795-ad15-00abdc7925fd@k13g2000vbq.googlegroups.com> <4cf3e9c3$0$13760$a729d347@news.telepac.pt>`

```
On Nov 30, 6:58 am, pt40br <pt4...@hotmail.com> wrote:
> Em 29-11-2010 17:12, tleaders...gmail.com escreveu:
>
…[25 more quoted lines elided]…
> Why? I don t know.

Files with variable length records need to have some way of knowing
where the next record starts. In this case it has added a record
header that specifies the length of that record. If you had written
several records then the bytes following the first would give the
length of the next record.

  |len|record data|len|record 2 data of some length|...

How else could it read the file as a series of records ?

With COBOL standard files the only way to avoid the |len| is to use
fixed length, the only way to avoid a terminator is to not use line
sequential.

One byte sequential does that.

Or use the CBL_ byte stream file routines:  CBL_CREATE_FILE
CBL_WRITE_FILE CBL_CLOSE_FILE.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: text file without CRLF

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "HeyBub" <heybub@NOSPAMgmail.com>

```
pt40br wrote:
> Em 29-11-2010 17:12, tleaders...gmail.com escreveu:
>>
…[28 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Try this. It works here (at least with LINE SEQUENTIAL files)

Change to:
FD FReg.
01  FReg-rec.
     02  FILLER OCCURS 1 TO 304 DEPENDING ON RECORD-LEN PIC X.


in your code, determine the length of the record

COMPUTE RECORD-LEN = FUNCTION STORED-CHAR-LENGTH (MYDATA)

then move your data to the record:
MOVE MYDATA TO FReg-rec.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: text file without CRLF

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-11-29T17:17:30-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<70ca1237-55b1-4827-980e-98b92923a7d5@r29g2000yqj.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<4cf3c969$0$13734$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <id0jio$q4$00$1@news.t-online.com> <4cf3d9d5$0$13731$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <4d21937a-d10e-4795-ad15-00abdc7925fd@k13g2000vbq.googlegroups.com> <4cf3e9c3$0$13760$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <qMOdnTop1sA-s2nRnZ2dnUVZ_gednZ2d@earthlink.com>`

```
On Nov 30, 11:52 am, "HeyBub" <hey...@NOSPAMgmail.com> wrote:
> pt40br wrote:
> > Em 29-11-2010 17:12, tleaders...gmail.com escreveu:
…[38 more quoted lines elided]…
> MOVE MYDATA TO FReg-rec.

There are only two problems with this:

1) It does not answer his requirement which is:

   """without CRLF at the end"""

The record is written with a terminator after the 'record-len', or
actually it may be after the last non-space, see 2.

2) It is completely unnecessary with LINE SEQUENTIAL. Spaces at the
end of the record are removed* and the record terminator is added
after the last non-space character.



* For Fujitsu COBOL it may be necessary to have
CBR_TRAILING_BLANK_RECORD=REMOVE
```

#### ↳ Re: text file without CRLF

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-11-29T09:41:20-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<e25a19fc-979f-4d57-9295-932a70539c54@p7g2000prb.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<4cf3c969$0$13734$a729d347@news.telepac.pt>`

```
On Nov 30, 4:40 am, pt40br <pt4...@hotmail.com> wrote:

> Someone can help me how to create a sequential file of variable size
> without CRLF at the end. I use Fujitsu Cobol V7
> Thanks

Normally files are written so that they can be read back. There must
be some indication of where records start and end. Fixed length
sequential needs no terminators because each record can be a fixed
length slice. Line sequential have variable sized records each
terminated by a CR/LF (or CR or LF depending on various factors).
Variable record sequential may have record headers that give the size
so the system knows where the next record starts.

If you want none of these, ie variable length but no terminators and
no headers then you can do this with a record sequential file with a
one byte record length.

      SELECT Output-Bytes ASSIGN Bytes-Name.

      FD Output-Bytes.
      01 One-Byte             PIC X.

This may be rather slow.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: text file without CRLF

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2010-11-29T12:14:25-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7ou7f651gimrdtrrb69i2464qekeeic2sp@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<4cf3c969$0$13734$a729d347@news.telepac.pt> <e25a19fc-979f-4d57-9295-932a70539c54@p7g2000prb.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Mon, 29 Nov 2010 09:41:20 -0800 (PST), Richard
<riplin@Azonic.co.nz> wrote:

>Normally files are written so that they can be read back. There must
>be some indication of where records start and end. Fixed length
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>so the system knows where the next record starts.

It's kind of a pain having so many standards though (many of them on
files on my Mac).   Check out http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newline .
```

```
of Burnside in 2008, now failing to be elected even as just councilor.

Earlier in 2010, Heather Kennett escaped police prosecution for a
vicious public attack on Burnside businessman Rick Powers for his
influence in the Burnside council. She stalked Mr. Powers at his
property to take an uncanny photo of the retired businessman.

In addition, Kennett was accused of having published numerous
anonymous articles on the internet on various blogs, petitions and
Usenet groups that attacked the Rick Powers team: Jane Howard, Robert
Paterson, Julian Carbone, Peter Pavan, Con Zacharakis and David
Lincoln. Despite the webpages were unable to be traced before, new
forensic technology has now traced the IP address to Kennett's work
computer at her Norwood office.

"Nobody messes with Rick Powers," a source close to Powers, who wished
to remain anonymous stated.

Julie Wade, sociological professor at the University of South
Australia classed Heather Kennett as "socially inept", claiming she
likely had an undiagnosed psychopathic disorder, which was
unsurprising given her career choice of journalism. He stated many
journalists decide to become reporters so they can gain power, and
that some like Kennett narcissistically abused others due to her own
childhood ridicule, humiliation, rejection, and other matters that
needed to be dealt with by a psychological "professional" and/or with
psychiatric drugs.

Allan Perry, the criminologist from the University of Adelaide
described Kennett's recent behaviour as "unusual" and "socially
deviant", likely to stem from her low self-esteem, self-centeredness,
and inappropriate anger.

A close family source to Heather Kennett who asked to remain unnamed
said Kennett was sexually abused by her father from the age of 12 to
19, and undervalued by her mother in her upbringing, and that both
Heather and her sister Chloe had engaged in prostitution as young
women, and that they had their own "issues" to work through.

Heather Kennett declined to comment when approached on her property.
```
